Special Article

Opinions on the View of Spoken Drama in Mr. Wang Bosheng's "Opinions on Theater Facilities" 94

— Zhang Daofan

Mr. Wang Bosheng recently wrote an "Opinion on Theater Facilities", which was published in the Central Daily News in early this month. There are indeed many commendable opinions in this opinion, but unfortunately, his view on spoken drama is inevitably too rash! Therefore, it has aroused great resentment from people who are working hard on spoken drama!

In the past ten days or so, I have received letters from five or six friends in Peiping and Shanghai (including Mr. Su Tang Huaiqiu and Luo Muhua), and I have also met many people in Nanjing who are working hard on spoken drama. They all expressed indignation at Mr. Wang's view of wiping out spoken drama and thinking that this road is impassable. They all said that they would write articles to refute it. Yesterday, I saw the supplement of the North China Daily and learned that Mr. Luo Muhua has publicly solicited opinions from readers on this matter. Mr. Sun Dezhong also published an article "On Spoken Drama and Peking Opera" in the Central Daily News. If it is not handled well, it will cause another war of words.

In fact, this matter is not worth the efforts of people who are working hard on spoken drama to oppose so vigorously. Mr. Wang Bosheng's view on spoken drama is inevitably a bit excessive. However, it is not surprising that Mr. Wang, who only knows how to work hard on new operas, made this view! This is just as unsurprising as some friends who work hard on spoken drama despise old operas as worthless!

"Spoken drama is art", I don't think it should be a problem. If this matter is still a problem in China in this era, wouldn't the Japanese laugh to death! How can the value of spoken drama art be wiped out by Mr. Wang's "Where is its artistic component?" a question? Some people's opinions are often subject to change. When Wang Guangsheng worked hard on spoken drama in those years, he also regarded spoken drama as art. When he felt that this road was impassable and worked hard on old operas, and later discovered that old operas needed to be improved and worked hard on new operas, he not only doubted that spoken drama was art. I am afraid that he also doubts old operas that are not new operas. Is this because Mr. Wang's belief in spoken drama is not firm and his research is not deep? Or is it that the art of spoken drama has fundamentally shaken? It is worth our careful study. How can people who pay attention to spoken drama doubt that spoken drama is art because of Mr. Wang's uncertain words?

In the eyes of Mr. Wang, who is working hard on new opera, of course, "New opera has a foundation", and the performance of spoken drama will have a new trend. Film art can get a new development. But in the eyes of people who are dedicated to spoken drama, it may be the opposite of Mr. Wang. Because when we look at the stage when spoken drama and film developed in the past, no country's spoken drama and film had a new trend of development because they had opera as a foundation. Even if Mr. Wang's words are correct, the foundation of the new opera is not yet determined when it will be built. If it cannot be built in twenty years, how can people who work hard on spoken drama "wait for the hare by the stump" and wait until twenty years later to borrow the foundation of the new opera to seek a new trend for spoken drama and a new development for film.

Mr. Wang feels that spoken drama is "Looking for another way out in the direction that this road is impassable." This is of course limited to Mr. Wang himself, or what Mr. Wang calls "us". Whether the road of spoken drama is passable or not, how can it be decided by Mr. Wang's understatement? How can people who work hard on spoken drama think that this road is impassable just because Mr. Wang thinks that "this road is impassable"? If so, it is too lacking in self-confidence. As for whether the new opera is sure to be passable? Or where will it lead to? It is difficult to predict at this moment. It all depends on the results of Mr. Wang's efforts in the future to determine. If the road of new opera is impassable again, Mr. Wang will of course find another way out. At that time, who knows that Mr. Wang's view on new opera will not be the same as today's view on spoken drama?

My opinion on this matter is just like this. What I hope most is: People who believe that "Spoken drama is art", believe that "The road of spoken drama is passable", believe that "The performance of spoken drama does not necessarily require a new opera to have a foundation to have a new trend", and believe that "Film art does not necessarily require a new opera to have a foundation to get a new development." should bury their heads, muster their courage, and move forward steadily. In the future, show the country the actual results. At that time, all the theories about spoken drama that are similar to Chu and not Chu can be defeated without attacking.

I also hope that Mr. Wang and Mr. Wang's "us" will be loyal and work hard for the early success of the new opera. There is no need to challenge all parties with unnecessary theories. If people who work hard on spoken drama do not work hard in practice, but only tout themselves by opposing old operas. Then we cannot call it boring to say that people who work hard on new opera and those who engage in old opera specialize in disparaging spoken drama to raise their own status! We should believe that: "Pointing out other people's shortcomings does not necessarily make your own strengths apparent"! Even if it can, this method cannot be considered clever. If everyone is already filled with miasma when the shadow of this new opera has not yet appeared and spoken drama has not yet fully developed. Then spoken drama will unfortunately be like what Mr. Wang said, it cannot be imitated in Europe and the United States in a hundred years. I am afraid that the new opera will never have a day when it will be superior to the Japanese. What is there to brag about? Do you really want to make the Japanese laugh to death?

Page 9

Local News

Sun Ke Returns from Touring Zhejiang Province's Scenic Spots 95

According to reports, Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke, accompanied by Vice Minister of Industry Liu Weichi and Legislative Yuan member Liang Hancao, traveled from Nanjing to Hangzhou on the 18th, and then toured the scenic spots around Wenzhou's Yandang Mountain. They returned to Shanghai from Hangzhou at 11 PM on the 23rd. In addition to sightseeing, Sun also inspected the highways in Zhejiang Province along the way, deeming the construction to be excellent. Due to the fatigue of the journey, he will stay in Shanghai for a few days before heading to Nanjing to attend the Legislative Yuan's regular meeting on the 29th. Sun met with reporters from various newspapers at his private residence on Columbia Road at 10 AM yesterday and made the following remarks:

European Situation

Reporters asked Sun about the international concern caused by Germany's recent rearmament, which has made countries such as Britain, France, and Italy uneasy. Sun stated that it is a natural trend for Britain, France, Italy, and other countries to feel that Germany's rearmament has caused tension in Europe. However, he does not expect a European war to break out immediately as a result. If it were to lead to a second world war, it would inevitably affect the entire world, as international relations are currently very close, and China would naturally be affected as well.

Eastern Road Incident

Regarding the Soviet Union's transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway, China has already issued a statement that the contract for the transfer has been signed, resulting in a significant loss of China's rights and interests. It is not yet known whether the government will submit this action by the Soviet Union, which disregards China's rights and interests, to the League of Nations for discussion.

Financial Public Bonds

In order to alleviate the decline of domestic industry and commerce, the Ministry of Finance plans to issue 100 million yuan in financial public bonds for the 24th year of the Republic. This has been decided by the Central Political Council and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review. The Legislative Yuan will propose the bond regulations for discussion at the regular meeting on the 29th, and Sun Ke has decided to attend the meeting in Nanjing beforehand. As for the drafting of the Legislative Yuan's bankruptcy law, it has already begun, and it is expected that opinions from all sectors will be solicited at the beginning of next month to avoid the drawbacks of "building a cart behind closed doors." Laws and regulations such as the labor law have also been initiated. To understand the actual conditions of labor in various regions, it has been decided to send personnel to conduct on-site inspections of various labor areas before drafting the laws.

Will Stay for One or Two Days Before Going to Hangzhou, and Plans to Visit North China for Inspection

Haiho Ship Sinks 98

Yesterday, various shipping companies in Shanghai received a telegram from the Hong Kong Customs, stating that the Haiho ship (Haiho, transliteration) sank the day before yesterday after hitting a reef at 25.42 degrees North latitude and 119.42 degrees East longitude. The location is on a major shipping route, so the Customs sent a telegram to broadcast to all ships at sea and to various shipping companies, informing ship owners who have not yet left port to pay special attention when passing through the area to avoid danger.

Arts and Antiquities Exhibition to Be Completed by the End of the Month; Tang Xifen Discusses Preparations for Shipping to England 99

According to the Central News Agency, the pre-exhibition of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art has been actively reviewed and selected by the Preparatory Committee, and most of the work has now been completed. Since a few days ago, the display of porcelain and other antiques has begun successively. A Central News Agency reporter met with the secretary of the committee, Tang Xifen, yesterday. According to him, the four British committee members still visit the exhibition to view the antiques every day. The evaluation of jade and silk tapestries has been completed, and they are now reviewing books and calligraphy. The initial intention of this exhibition of antiques was to collect a wide range of items, so the display cabinets were increased from 64 to 92. However, due to stricter selection criteria recently, many of the more valuable items have been deselected, so the antiques on display are not as numerous as initially hoped, and the display cabinets are somewhat excessive. They are now accelerating the display, which can be completed before the 31st. Protection and fire prevention measures at the venue are in place, especially regarding fire safety. Chemical fire extinguishers, water buckets, fire hydrants, and fire alarm telephones are all installed in appropriate locations. It is rumored that the British warship Suffolk will be used to transport the antiques, but this has not yet been decided. Generally, the storage hold of a warship is not as well-suited as that of a merchant ship. Therefore, when the Suffolk arrives in Shanghai, the committee will send personnel to board the ship for inspection. If it is not suitable, merchant ships will still be used for transportation. The price of admission tickets after the opening has not yet been determined, but the exhibition hours have been set from 9:00 AM to 4:30 PM. Tickets will no longer be sold after 4:30 PM, but those in the venue can view the exhibits until 6:00 PM. From 6:00 PM to 8:00 PM, the venue will be cleaned. As for the shipment of antiques to England, tenders have been invited for the manufacture of iron boxes. Dasing Factory has already sent a sample box, made of black iron sheet with brass strips and nails, locked on three sides, which is quite sturdy and beautiful. The inside bottom is equipped with springs to prevent the antiques in the box from being damaged by shocks.

Shanghai Suburban Agricultural Association Held Its Inaugural Meeting Yesterday; Niu Yongjian, Huang Yanpei, and Others Served as Chairmen; Tai Shuangqiu, Tao Zhihsing, and Others Gave Speeches; Discussed the Constitution and Passed the Outline of Work 102

The Shanghai Suburban Rural Work Association held its inaugural meeting yesterday at the Yutang Provincial Public Education Hall. The opening ceremony started at 9 AM, and the constitution and work outline were discussed in the afternoon. Details are as follows:

Attendees

Those in attendance included Niu Yongjian and Niu Changyao from the Yutang Public Education Hall, Huang Yanpei, Jiang Wenyu, Yao Huiquan, and Lu Shu'ang from the Vocational Education Society, Tao Zhihsing and Huang Jingwan from the Public Education Assistance Association, Tai Shuangqiu from the Great China University, Yu Qingtang from the Wuxi Provincial Education and Commercial College, Yang Shusun from Jinan University, Shanghai County Magistrate Pan Zhongjia, Director of Education Bureau Zhu Changlin, Agricultural Education Officer Zhang Yi, Director of the County Public Education Hall Jin Zuobin, Zhang Jingye from the Shanghai County Party Headquarters, Wang Kuisheng from the Gaoqiao Improvement Zone, and guests Zhao Guangtao and others, totaling more than 200 people.

Chairman's Report

The meeting started at 10 AM. Niu Yongjian, Huang Yanpei, and Jiang Wenyu were elected as the presidium. After performing the ceremonial rites, Chairman Huang Yanpei delivered a speech, saying that the Shanghai Suburban Agricultural Association held its inaugural meeting today, and the future of the association is infinitely hopeful. The work of the association focuses on the word "association," which means sincerity, and the word "progress," which means vitality. Next, Niu Xingwo reported on the preparations, saying that the association began preparations in mid-January, decided on a work plan, sought membership methods, and appointed preparatory members to be responsible for preparations. There are currently eight organizational members and more than 200 individual members.

Speeches from All Sectors

Next, Zhang Jingye of the Shanghai County Party Headquarters delivered a speech, expressing great hope for the association, and hoping to strengthen contact in the work. Next, Shanghai County Magistrate Pan Zhongjia delivered a speech, saying that rural improvement should theoretically be handled by the government, but the government's capacity is weak at present. He is very grateful that local enthusiasts have come together to take responsibility for improvement. As for improving the countryside, the work is very large, and it is necessary to organize the people first in order to be effective. Next, there were speeches: (1) Yu Qingtang said that Yutang has been managed and improved by Mr. Niu Yongjian, and it is significantly different from the past. All kinds of progress have been made, and now Mr. Niu is committed to the Shanghai suburbs, and his success must be great. (2) Tai Shuangqiu said that among the entire problems of China, the most important is the people's livelihood problem. Therefore, those engaged in rural work should focus on the people's livelihood problem. (2) Promote agricultural products and promote sideline industries. (3) The whole country should use rural native products as much as possible. There were also speeches by Tao Zhihsing and Zheng Xigu, etc.

Discussion Issues

The discussion meeting started at 1 PM. The preliminary measures for improving cotton production were discussed and it was resolved to handle three items. Next, the constitution was discussed, and it was revised and passed item by item. Finally, the outline of the work of the Shanghai Suburban Rural Work Association was discussed. It took a long time to pass, and the outline is as follows: (1) Principles: (1) The scope of work extends from Shanghai County to other counties. (2) Investigation is the basis for research and experimentation. (3) Combine doing, learning, and teaching, and focus on doing. (4) Transform the countryside, and the three aspects of economy, culture, and politics should be linked together, especially the economy. (5) Those who know should teach others, and those who do not know have the obligation to learn. (6) Schools, social education institutions, and cooperatives should be the basis for work. (7) Work closely with various agencies and organizations. (8) Train local talents as much as possible for the purpose of training local people. (9) Carrying out rural undertakings should not increase the burden on farmers. (10) Society and schools should be integrated, and social education and school education should be integrated. (11) Grasp the existing group life, and start with education. (12) Use the latest means of transportation to transport culture, so that culturally backward areas can catch up with the forefront of the times. (13) Valley's facilities are not only for passive adaptation, but should pay attention to active transformation. (14) When planning work, design should be the main focus, but attention should be paid to the following points: A. Attention should be paid to the following in each design: (1) Work allocation; (2) Time allocation; (3) Talent allocation; (4) Funding allocation. B. The standing point of the design should be from the bottom up, and cooperate with politics as much as possible. C. Each design should pay attention to the universality and particularity of the problem. D. It should go from sponsorship to self-help, guidance to self-guidance, and passive to active. E. Based on the principles of mutual assistance and cooperation, the people should have a concrete organization and discipline, and manage and train each other. Through this method, the people should be united, the people should be promoted, and they should have the ability to automatically govern themselves and solve their lives as a whole.

Work Objectives

2. Objectives: A. Unification, unify political education, unify livelihood education, unify literacy education, unify health education, unify civic education. B. Popularization, popularize children's education, popularize youth education, popularize adult education, popularize women's education. 3. Career: A. Those related to the unification aspect: (1) Livelihood education, A. In terms of agricultural production, improve the inherent farming skills, promote emerging agriculture, pay attention to seed selection, fertilization, and prevention and control of diseases and insect pests. Other horticulture and animal husbandry should also apply agricultural science to improve production, so that farmers can receive the minimum agricultural science in agricultural affairs. B. In terms of agricultural economy, use cooperative methods, educate farmers, and organize farmers, so that farmers can get considerable remedies under the condition of bankruptcy. C. In terms of rural crafts, attention should be paid to agricultural product processing, agricultural product manufacturing, and the improvement of farmers' handicrafts, and other sideline industries should be promoted to enrich their economic production capacity. (2) Political education, in accordance with the central political guidelines, give the necessary and possible subsidies in education. (3) Literacy education, A. Eliminate school walls, break traditional concepts, and integrate school education with social education. B. Mobilize all primary school students, implement the newly invented "little teacher system", and popularize children's education as much as possible. C. Mobilize all literate and adult people, implement the newly invented "training system", and popularize adult education as much as possible. D. Mobilize all intellectuals to guide the advancement of popular education. E. Unite all levels of normal schools and primary and secondary schools, and try to run popular education to expand the teaching staff and implement mobile education. G. Implement electrification education. (4) Health education, A. Implement the rural health care system, with health care workers in each village, health care stations in each district, and health care hospitals in the whole county (run by the hospital). B. Pay attention to environmental sanitation, focusing on street and family hygiene. C. Pay attention to school health, focusing on physical examination and health facilities. D. Pay attention to obstetric hygiene, focusing on newborn publicity and midwifery education. (5) Autonomous education, A. Unite local autonomous personnel and complete autonomous organizations at all levels. B. Organize fire brigades to assist in the progress of local undertakings. C. Organize youth service groups to cultivate the spirit of hard work for the public. D. Use family-style education to awaken people's national consciousness. B. Regarding the popularization aspect, (1) Popularize children's education (under the age of fourteen), A. In the elementary level, use the forward-looking literacy education method, implement the little teacher system, and provide free schooling. B. The advanced level is divided into two groups: (1) University-bound group, educated according to the regular primary school method; (2) Vocational group, for rural occupations, educated according to the living school method. (2) Popularize youth education, A. Young men aged sixteen to twenty should be specially trained to cultivate quantity. B. In addition to following the curriculum of civil schools, the training subjects should especially focus on agronomy, common sense of citizenship, military training, new life, and the organization and implementation of health cooperatives. (3) Popularize adult education, and the training methods are the same as youth education. (4) Popularize women's education, A. In addition to the civil school curriculum, the selected subjects are agronomy, handicrafts, gauze, sewing, and weaving. B. Compulsory subjects: the tasks and common sense of female citizens, military training common sense, new life, health (medical common sense and nursing), cooperation, and domestic administration.

Implementation Measures

4. Measures, A. Handling agencies—division of labor and cooperation, (1) Direct agricultural education agencies, A. From Minhang to Beiqiao, the Minhang Education Center is responsible; B. From Caohejing to Beiqiao, the Agricultural Society and Zhuanqiao Public Education Center are responsible; C. From Beiqiao to the Songjiang boundary, the Yutang Public Education Center is responsible. (2) Indirect agricultural education agencies, A. From Minhang to Beiqiao, the normal school, junior high school, central primary school, and Beiqiao Primary School are responsible; B. From Caohejing to Beiqiao, Shanghai Middle School and Primary School are responsible; C. From Beiqiao to the Songjiang boundary, the farm and Qiangshu Primary School are responsible. D. All primary schools along the road must have a unified education area, conduct detailed investigations, and form an education network in order to proceed in stages. (3) Selected education assistance agencies, the roads of Hu-Min and Shang-Song are assisted by the Party, government, education, and hospitals. B. Guidance agency, research and experimentation guidance, (1) The association sets up an office in the Yutang Education Center. In addition to handling daily association affairs, it also hires experts to discuss and study the practical problems of various rural work and design plans. (2) Set up supervisors to guide the progress and investigate the progress and report to the competent authorities for assessment. (3) Prepare a training course or training class to train rural workers. C. Funding, (1) The competent authority shall stipulate according to the scope of its business. (2) All agency staff and school teachers who are engaged in rural work are volunteers. (3) All rural construction funds should be the responsibility of the local government. (4) If necessary, request the government for supplementary funds.

4 Million Yuan Loan for Guiding the Huai River; Sassoon Yangxing Has Fully Paid the Loan; The Huai River Guidance Committee Cancels the Issuance of New Public Bonds 106

According to Ta Kung Pao, in order to carry out the work of guiding the Huai River, the Huai River Guidance Committee previously borrowed 9 million yuan from the Central Gengzi Indemnity Committee. The Sino-British Gengzi Indemnity Board of Directors formally approved the loan, but the Huai River Guidance Committee urgently needed huge amounts of cash for various Huai River guidance projects. Therefore, it borrowed a huge amount of money from the loan department of Sassoon Yangxing in Shanghai. After consultation, both parties have agreed that the Sino-British Gengzi Indemnity will be used as collateral. The amount is stipulated as 4 million yuan in Chinese currency, with an annual interest rate of six percent. It will be repaid in ten installments from January 1, 1935, until the entire amount is paid off by 1946. The contract was signed and established last month. It is heard that Sassoon Yangxing paid the entire amount last week, and the new public bonds that the Huai River Guidance Committee planned to issue have been canceled.

Transportation Truck Industry: Measures for Collecting Aviation Donations 112

Submits Request to the Municipal Government for Approval

The Shanghai Collection Team Headquarters of the China Aviation Association, in order to raise aviation national salvation donations, previously sent a letter to the Shanghai Transportation Truck Industry Association to collect aviation national salvation donations. After receiving the letter, the association expressed great sympathy and convened a meeting of all its members on the 19th of this month for discussion. It was resolved and passed to collect aviation national salvation donations. All freight trucks in the city, regardless of black or yellow license plates, will be charged six yuan per month until 100,000 yuan has been collected. This has been reported in the newspapers. It is reported that the General Team Headquarters has specially formulated ten measures for the collection of aviation national salvation donations in the industry and sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Government for approval and reply so that they can be informed and collection can begin immediately. The measures are as follows: (1) The China Aviation Association has formulated these measures to raise funds for national salvation through aviation; (2) Each freight truck will be charged six yuan per month for aviation national salvation donations; (3) Freight truck companies will pay the aviation national salvation donations collected according to the number of vehicles to the Shanghai Collection Team Headquarters of the China Aviation Association every month; (4) All freight trucks, regardless of black or yellow license plates, are subject to collection; (5) Each freight truck company must post the collection of aviation national salvation donations measures in each truck company and on trucks for customers to read; (6) The aviation national salvation donations collected by each freight truck company are limited to 100,000 yuan; (7) When the China Aviation Association receives payments from the freight truck industry, it will print a three-part receipt for the aviation national salvation donations collected from the freight truck industry and issue them separately for collection; (8) After the China Aviation Association starts collecting aviation national salvation donations from the freight truck industry, it may send personnel to inspect at any time. If there is any concealment or failure to report or wait and see, it will request the government to withhold licenses; (9) The China Aviation Association shall announce the number of aviation national salvation donations received from the freight truck industry every month; (10) These measures shall be submitted to the government for approval and implementation. The General Team Headquarters yesterday received 200 yuan in aviation national salvation donations from Mrs. Mei Huaquan and Ms. Jiang Hezheng of the Shanghai Women's Association, and receipts and thank-you letters have been issued.

Shanghai County Baojia Organization Statistics 113

The Shanghai County Government has completed the organization of Baojia in accordance with orders. The Baojia chiefs of each township are selected and appointed by the county to serve. Huge Ship of Changxing Company to Arrive in Shanghai 114

Empress of Britain to Arrive on the 29th

The "Empress of Britain" of Changxing Company, the most beautiful of all the ships owned by the company, will arrive in Shanghai next Friday. This time, it carries 500 passengers on a world tour. It set sail from New York in January and will arrive in Southampton, England, on May 27th. Every time it arrives at a port, it is according to the scheduled date. It is expected to arrive at Songkou at 6:00 a.m. next Friday (29th). Every time it arrives at a place, there are countless people who ask for permission to board the ship for sightseeing, but for the sake of the safety of the passengers, the number of people allowed to visit is strictly limited. The ship has a gross tonnage of 42,500 tons, a displacement of 63,750 tons, a length of 758 feet, and a width of 97 and a half feet. Its engine can generate 64,000 horsepower. The mast is 208 feet above the loading waterline. The total length of its promenade deck is almost equal to the bypass of an average golf course, totaling 26,000 feet. The number of guests that its public rooms and rooms can accommodate is unparalleled. Therefore, crossing the Atlantic and sailing in tropical waters, its comfort is far beyond that of other ships. The ship has two large swimming pools. On the lower deck, there is a gym and a beauty salon. The entrance and exit of the front deck. The ship was launched by the Prince of England in 1930 and made its maiden voyage in May 1931. It has created many records over the years. Before leaving New York for a world tour this time, when sailing in the West Indies, the number of times passengers made telephone calls from the ship's radio department to the shore was the highest ever recorded by any ship on any day. This is the most recent record created by the ship.

North China Automobile Company Workers Demand Legal Dissolution, Negotiating with the Capital's Agent Lawyer This Morning 118

The North China Automobile Company on South Xun Road is experiencing poor economic turnover and owes more than 80,000 yuan to gasoline companies and automobile companies. Unable to maintain, after a de facto shutdown, manager Qian Wenhao absconded and disappeared. Thirty-four automobiles were removed by the claimants. The water, electricity, and telephone were also cut off by the water and electricity companies. The company's 72 drivers, due to the capital's situation, not only owed wages for February and March, which were not paid, but also the deposit would be difficult to obtain. Therefore, they decided on a solution in a meeting yesterday: (1) The deposit paid by the workers, 50 yuan per person, has been used by the company and should be guaranteed by the company; (2) Whether the company continues to operate or not should be notified to the workers in detail with concrete measures; (3) During the shutdown, the company should maintain the workers' meals; (4) During this shutdown period, wages should be borne by the capital, and substitute workers should be paid half the amount, or legally dissolved, and representatives were elected to negotiate with the capital's agent lawyer Chen Maoxuan this morning.

French Concession Changes Tow Truck Regulations 120

The Shanghai French Concession Board of Directors has made slight changes to the regulations for managing tow trucks. The order has been promulgated by the French Consul General in Shanghai. The amended articles of the Shanghai Public Works Bureau's Regulations for the Control of Tow Trucks are recorded below: "The length of the tow truck and its cargo shall not exceed eight meters and five centimeters. Its width and its cargo shall also not exceed the width of the front truck, but if the tow truck is towed by a special type of locomotive, its width and its cargo shall not exceed two meters and five centimeters." These articles have recently been announced by the consulate for public knowledge.

Eleven Young Girls Imprisoned 123

Thugs Forcibly Prevent Return, Family Members Sue to the Court for Arrest

Farmers Yang Dengrong and Qin Qiqing from Taixing, due to rural bankruptcy and a large family, found it difficult to support themselves. Therefore, around June of the 20th year of the Republic of China, they were brought to Shanghai by a fellow villager, Mrs. Chen, one after another: Yang Dengrong's daughter Luo Ying, Qin Qiqing's daughter Su Zhen, Qin Qiliang's niece Gui'er, Qiu Hefei's niece Gai Zhen, Qiu's sister-in-law Guang Ying, Qi Henggao's daughter Ruzi, Qi Fubao's daughter Liuzi, Qi Xu's eldest daughter, Qiu Shenshan's sister Fenzi, Li Tianshou's sister Fenzi, and Wang's daughter Xiaobao, eleven girls in total (all aged between fourteen and sixteen years). They were introduced as female workers to the Huafeng and Yong'an factories, and lived and ate at Mrs. Chen's house. Unexpectedly, around January of this year, Mrs. Chen became seriously ill and unable to care for them, so she sent people to the countryside, ordering the family heads of each family to come to Shanghai quickly to take them back, so as to avoid being displaced. Upon hearing the news, Yang Dengrong and others immediately made an appointment with the family heads to come to Shanghai. Unexpectedly, upon arriving in Shanghai, Mrs. Chen had already died. Just as the family heads were preparing to take their daughters back, Zhao Guangzhi, whose original name was Zhou Chengxin, who lived in Yinghua Lane on Roberts Road, instigated female gangsters Sister Liu to lead more than ten male and female thugs to interfere and prevent them from taking the girls back. Yang Dengrong and others, seeing this, urgently tried to reason with them, but were immediately attacked and beaten by the thugs, injuring Qi Xu. Yang Dengrong and others are all simple and weak villagers, and in a foreign land with no relatives, they repeatedly negotiated to take them back, but were all unreasonably prevented. Yang and others, fearing their ferocity, did not dare to argue, and sought help everywhere. They were directed to Zhu Honglie's Law Firm, where they explained the details. Yesterday morning, Attorney Zhu wrote a complaint on their behalf, reporting to the Prosecutor's Office of the District Court, accusing the defendants Zhao Guangzhi (who is reportedly in custody in the District Court detention center for another case) and Sister Liu of obstructing freedom and violent assault, requesting that the police be ordered to quickly arrest the defendants and severely punish them according to law, and order them to hand over the daughters of the plaintiffs, so that they can be taken back and reunited, to complete the family relationship. It was also said that the defendants dared to imprison the actions of the plaintiffs' daughters and forcibly separate them from their families under the flag of the Qing Tian Bai Ri, making it impossible for the family to reunite, and dared to commit assault and injury, which was extremely illegal. It is rumored that the defendants have further plans to hide or sell the eleven daughters of the plaintiffs in separate locations. Because the plaintiffs' daughters are all young girls around the age of 20, if they are hidden, the plaintiffs will not be able to take steps to recover them, which is extremely dangerous. They beg the court to quickly conduct an investigation of the injuries and immediately order the police to go to the address and arrest them, and hand over the eleven daughters of the plaintiffs for each family to take back, to complete the family relationship and maintain the law. Furthermore, the plaintiffs have been in Shanghai for a long time and their funds have been exhausted. If the delay continues, they will starve to death in a foreign land. Therefore, they respectfully request the court to take swift action. After receiving the complaint, the court immediately convened a prosecutor to open a court, questioned each of the plaintiffs one by one, verified the wounds of Qi Xu, and dispatched police to cooperate with the plaintiffs to identify and arrest them.

In the garden at the south end of the Hongqiao Airport in West Shanghai, at about 0:30 a.m. yesterday, two robbers dressed in yellow military uniforms, wearing yellow military caps, and speaking with a northern accent suddenly came. Each held a Mauser pistol and broke in. One robber stood guard at the door, and the other robber entered. It is reported that his life is in danger. Then, they inspected the scene and returned to the station to report.

Clerk Zhu Xifan Neglects and Issues Release Ticket to Release Thief, Zhu Xifan Ordered to Be Dismissed from Duty, Arrest Warrant Issued After Thief Escapes 128

The thief Chen Linsheng, a native of Ningbo, was arrested in the Public Concession in the spring of last year for committing a robbery case. He was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment by the First Special Court. Later, the French police found that Chen had also committed a theft in the French Concession, so they sent a detective to the First Special Court to transfer Chen to the Second Special Court and filed a public prosecution. Unexpectedly, after the decision was finalized in the two trials, Zhu Xifan, the clerk in charge of the High Third Branch, neglected to investigate the case file in detail and rashly reported to the judge in charge to issue a release ticket to release Chen. Chen was lucky enough to be released from prison and escaped, and disappeared without a trace. When the High Third Branch discovered this, it sent police to pursue and arrest him, but was unable to find him. Liang, the president of the High Third Branch, believed that Zhu had neglected his duties, mistakenly released the thief, and obstructed official duties, so he immediately ordered Zhu to be detained for investigation and ordered him to be released on bail pending investigation. At that time, because the case was confidential, it was not disclosed. It is now reported that the case has come to an end. In addition to issuing an arrest warrant for Chen, Liang, the president of the High Third Branch, ordered Zhu Xifan to be dismissed from his position a few days ago to show punishment.

Opening of Longhua Temple - Restoring Its Former Glory of Decades Ago 131

Longhua Temple in this city is a famous ancient temple in Shanghai, said to have been built during the Chiwu period. Next to the temple is a seven-story pagoda. Throughout history, incense offerings have been abundant. During the mid-Qing Dynasty, the number of monks from all directions seeking lodging at the temple reached six to seven hundred. Since the beginning of the Republic of China, it has suffered from repeated military conflicts, causing the temple to fall into disrepair and the monks to disperse. After Abbot Yuanzhao took over, he failed to uphold the monastic rules and sold temple property. The Arhat and Constellation Halls within the temple were also destroyed by fire, with broken doors and windows, in a deplorable state. Last spring, the Buddhist Association hired the Venerable Xingkong, an elder monk from Mount Emei (a former Qing Dynasty scholar), as the abbot of the temple. He renovated the temple and raised a large sum of money to rebuild the Arhat and Constellation Halls, as well as the east and west bell and drum towers, on their original sites, giving them a completely new appearance. Over the past year, more than forty to fifty thousand yuan has been spent. The temple now has more than three hundred monks, restoring it to its former glory of decades ago. Now that the spring is bright and the peach blossoms are red and the willows are green, the people of Shanghai are flocking to visit in large numbers. Yesterday was Sunday, so the number of tourists was even greater.

Thugs Forcibly Take a Woman on Hongnanshan Road 135

Claiming He Paid Twenty Yuan for Her - Woman Cried for Help, But No One Dared to Respond

At 10:10 AM yesterday, police officer Li Deming, No. 28 post, from the Zhongxing Road Police Station of the Zhabei New Gate Sub-bureau, received a report from Madam Chen Cai, who lives at No. 48 Hongnanshan Road in the vicinity, claiming that last night, thugs Gao Quanlang and others drove her husband away and forcibly took her as their wife. After receiving the report, Officer Li immediately went to the scene, brought Gao Quanlang and Chen Cai to the station, and transferred them to the New Gate Sub-bureau. According to Chen Cai's testimony to Bureau Officer Huang, she is 28 years old, from Liyang, and currently resides at No. 48 Hongnanshan Road (i.e., in the middle of Gonghexin Road). A few years ago, due to the riots of the Big Sword Society in her hometown, her husband, Zhu Yaoyue, was captured and injured while carrying ammunition. Although he escaped back from Tianjin, he died a few days later. After her husband's death, she married Mu Yisan as his wife for four years. On the 12th day of the lunar first month this year, Cai brought her from her hometown to Shanghai, residing on Hongnanshan Road. Cai is 30 years old and makes a living as a steward for others. Unexpectedly, thugs Gao Quanlang and Gao Jilang, who lived across the street, wanted to forcibly take her as their wife. Last night (i.e., the night before), Mr. Gao treated Cai Yisan to wine at the intersection of Gonghexin Road and Hongnanshan Road and told him that he could either do things openly or secretly. Openly meant that Cai Yisan should give up Chen Cai to others and never come to Hongnanshan Road again. Secretly meant dealing with him with knives. Being forced by them, Cai Yisan abandoned her and left at around 10 PM, disappearing. That night, Gao Quanlang came to sleep with her in the same bed. Because she was unwilling, she cried for help. Unexpectedly, the residents there were so afraid of the thugs that none dared to respond. During the rape, she was slapped in the face, breaking her nose, resulting in bloodstains all over her body as proof. They also placed a sharp knife about four to five inches long next to the pillow to scare her into silence. Gao Quanlang testified that he is 27 years old, from Chongming, and lives at No. 42 Hongnanshan Road. Cai sold the Cai woman to him, so he gave her twenty yuan last night. Therefore, it was proper for him to sleep with her and not forcibly take someone else's wife. He did not know when her husband left. After examining the testimony, the interrogating officer determined that the case involved the rape of someone else's wife and contained elements of deception. This sub-bureau was not able to handle it and therefore transferred it to the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

After Ren Jianpei's Death, His Concubine Sues to Dispute Her Status - Sues the First Wife to Recognize Her as a Family Member - Court Orders Investigation and Rescheduled Hearing 136

Huang Peiyan, a Cantonese Panyu woman residing at No. 87 Tianshou Lane, Keming Road, Hongkou, age 33, recently filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against Ren Feng, the wife of the deceased Ren Jianpei, from Heshan, concerning a dispute over her status. According to Huang Peiyan's complaint, she began cohabitating with Ren Jianpei in 1928. On August 29 of the following year, Ren officially recognized her as a family member. She bore two sons who both died young. In the year before last, she gave birth to a daughter named Huanzhen. On December 27 of last year, while Ren was at home, the first wife, Ren Feng, suddenly came and created a great disturbance, damaging property and forcibly dragging her husband away. This caused her husband to become ill from anger and die on January 8 of this year. Upon hearing the bad news, she rushed to the coffin with her daughter to mourn. However, the first wife and her husband's brothers refused to let her enter and even drove her away. At that time, she was still pregnant and Huanzhen was very young. For safety reasons, she had to endure it temporarily and did not dare to resist, returning with tears. Now she has given birth to another daughter, Yufang. In grief, she filed a lawsuit, requesting that the defendant, Ren Feng, be summoned to testify and be judged to confirm that she is one of Ren Jianpei's family members, and that the eldest and second daughters are Ren Jianpei's biological daughters. However, Ren Feng hired lawyer Gu Yongquan to file a defense, denying that Ren Huang was Ren Jianpei's concubine. She claimed that she had been married to Ren Jianpei for nearly 30 years and had a son. The couple's relationship was always very close. Her husband always returned home at night and never sought pleasure outside. This was known to all their relatives and friends. Last month, when her husband passed away, a stranger named Ren Huang suddenly sent a letter, claiming to be her husband's concubine and demanding a share of the inheritance. Because she ignored it, she is now suing to confirm her status. The evidence she presented is insufficient to prove her claim. According to Guangdong customs, all newborns must have their birthdates reported to the ancestral hall and entered into the family genealogy, and lanterns must be lit and a banquet held for relatives and friends at the ancestral hall during the Lantern Festival. If the plaintiff's two daughters were born to her late husband, why were these customs not followed? Furthermore, on August 26 of last year, her late husband held a birthday celebration for his mother and hosted a banquet at the Taotao Restaurant on Wuchang Road. Why did the plaintiff not come to dance and offer a toast? As for the claim that she brought her daughter to the family to mourn after her late husband's death and was driven away, this is also false. Even if her late husband had a clandestine relationship with her, it can only be considered a cohabitation relationship, not protected by law. How could she claim to have obtained the status of a family member? The lawsuit should be rejected. Yesterday, Judge Yu opened the court for interrogation. The defendant, Ren Feng, claimed to be ill and did not appear, represented by lawyer Gu Yongquan. The plaintiff, Ren Huang, appeared with her lawyer, Sun Biwu, and presented her case, submitting a red paper written by Ren Jianpei acknowledging her as his concubine and all related letters. After Judge Yu reviewed the evidence, he ordered the case to be investigated further and rescheduled for a later hearing.

A Tourist Commits Suicide at the New Asia Hotel 137

Leaving Only an English Name - Died After Being Sent to the Hospital

A middle-aged man speaking Cantonese checked into room No. 63 of the New Asia Hotel on North Sichuan Road the day before yesterday. He only left an English name (Kong TsuVung), Kang Zuofeng (transliteration). Yesterday afternoon, a hotel attendant, noticing no activity in the room, became suspicious and managed to open the door. Abundant Production of "Noodle Fish" in Wusong 139

More Than One Hundred Loads Can Be Caught Every Day

Since spring, "noodle fish" have been produced in the waters outside the Sancha Estuary in Wusong. This is an annual marine product, and there are quite a few fishing boat owners who rely on this for a living. These "noodle fish" were discovered as early as the end of the first month of the lunar calendar. However, the output was very small. Initially, only three to five catties were caught per tide, so the price was quite high, requiring seven or eight copper coins per ounce. But the quantity was very small and could only be sold in Wusong. Until recently, the output has been abundant and the price has also decreased greatly. Seventy to eighty loads, or even more than one hundred loads, can be caught per tide. Each catty sells for only about 200 cash. In recent days, various fish shops in Wusong have packed the large quantities of "noodle fish" they receive daily into buckets, covered them with ice, and transported them to Shanghai for sale. Because these "noodle fish" are white like silver strips, taste quite delicious, and have no bones, everyone loves them, so there is no need to worry about the market being sluggish.

Record of the Annual General Meeting of Shareholders of the China Merchants Electric Power Company Held Yesterday 141

Lu Bohong Reports on Business Conditions - Du Yuesheng and Others Elected as Directors and Supervisors

According to the Dagong News Agency, the Shanghai China Merchants Electric Power Company held its annual general meeting of shareholders at 2 PM yesterday at the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association on Tibet Road. More than 200 shareholders attended. Manager Lu Bohong reported on the company's business conditions for the 23rd year of the Republic (i.e., the company's 17th year), as well as the company's construction projects. Dividends were distributed, and directors and supervisors were elected. Details are as follows:

Business Conditions: At the start of the meeting, six people, including standing directors Wang Yiting, Gu Xinyi, Zhang Xiaoliang, Du Yuesheng, Yao Ziruo, and manager Lu Bohong, served as the presidium. After formalities, manager Lu Bohong reported, stating that the company had added two million yuan in capital according to the resolutions of the previous shareholders' meeting and had begun collecting it in small amounts since July of last year. The full amount has already been collected. However, due to the bankruptcy of rural areas in mainland China and the economic downturn in various industries, the company has inevitably been affected. Public utilities should prioritize serving the convenience of citizens, and the company does not hesitate to make sacrifices and continues to actively expand its facilities. Revenue has not decreased compared to previous years, which is comforting. However, since increasing tram fares last year, revenue has actually decreased, which is also due to the poor economic situation.

Construction Projects: Construction is divided into two parts: electric power and trams. Regarding electric power, the capacity of the power plant was previously insufficient. Last year, a transformer substation was built on Zhongshan Road to connect to the power grid in Zhabei for supplementation. This equipment was completed last winter and started generating electricity on January 4 of this year. Due to a malfunction in the diesel engine at the Fahua plant, a high-voltage cable was used to pass through Hongqiao Road and connect to the Zhongshan Road line. To address the insufficient original power generation equipment, a new plant was planned according to the shareholders' meeting resolution. It was decided to build the new plant on the company's existing site, west of Shenjia Garden along the Bund and east of the Inland Water Company. Three 15,000-kilowatt steam turbine generators and four boilers will be installed, which are expected to be completed in the 26th year of the Republic [1937]. Regarding trams, a new line was added to the Xiaobeimen power line. New tracks were replaced in the section from Zhonghua Road Ximen to Shangwenmen. The project was completed at the end of last year. New tracks were replaced and roadbed and pavement were constructed between Shangwenmen and Xiaodongmen, completing the work in November last year.

Page 12

The section at the Huangjia Que Road intersection, which was originally a single track, was converted to a double track in June last year. The section at Damatou was rerouted to Lime Road, but the project has not yet been completed. Ten new motorized trams and four trailers were added this year. Concrete steel frame high poles were replaced for the tram lines along the Outer Bund.

Election of Directors and Supervisors: After the distribution of dividends was completed, the election of 17 directors began. Wang Yiting, Du Yuesheng, Yao Mulian, Yao Ziruo, Gu Xinyi, Zhang Xiaoliang, Huang Hanzhi, Ye Hongying, Zhu Zhiyao, Zhu Yinjiang, Ling Bohua, Yu Baoqing, Liu Hongyuan, Zhu Jilin, Feng Bingnan, Wang Yunfu, and Lu Yingen were elected. Five supervisors were elected: Zhang Wenbin, Zhu Luyi, Wen Xianglin, Jia Jiying, and Li Zuhua. After reports were presented, refreshments were served, and the meeting adjourned at approximately 6 PM.

(C) During the two months of the solicitation campaign, hold two National Products Promotion Weeks, the first three weeks after the opening and the second one week before the closing. It was resolved that since the citywide student national product swearing-in ceremony has been rescheduled to April 18, the exhibition should be rescheduled accordingly. The Repeated Offender, Bandit Wang Yougen, and Others Arrested 147

Jin Hengming Also Confesses to Robbery; Both Criminals Handed Over to the Headquarters Yesterday for Legal Action

Dong Mingde, the leader of the detective squad of the 16th Precinct of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, learned the other day that Wang Yougen, a native of Pudong who resides at No. 53 Ruiji Lane, Jiaxing Road, in the Public Concession and runs an "Swallow's Nest," had, on the tenth day of the first lunar month of this year, at midnight, armed himself and, together with Jin Hengming, a native of Zhenjiang who formerly ran a printing business at No. 44 Mingyuanfang, Huade Road, robbed pedestrians of their property near Xiaoshijie in the city. He also robbed a certain cigarette paper shop on Yidingpan Road of 72 yuan in foreign currency and 20 jiao in small change in October of last year. At the same time, he also learned of the robbery of banknotes from the Wanfeng Rice Shop at No. 750, the intersection of Xibaoxing Road and London Road in Zhabei. Furthermore, he learned that Wang and his gang were going to gather at a certain restaurant near the Nine-Bend Bridge in the City Temple to attempt a robbery. He immediately reported this information to the captain of the general team, Lu Ying, and the director of the 16th Precinct, Huang Junfu, who immediately dispatched team leaders Han Ruisheng and Yuan Haishan, along with a large number of detectives including Guo Shiqing, Cheng Songlin, and Yu Maolong, all disguised as peddlers, to secretly surround the area near the Nine-Bend Bridge at around 4 p.m. the other day. After a while, the bandit Wang Gen indeed arrived and passed by the Nine-Bend Bridge, where the officers bravely stepped forward, arrested him, and took him into custody. After interrogation, Wang confessed directly to the robberies mentioned above and admitted to spending the stolen money without hesitation. He also revealed the hideouts of his accomplices who were still at large. The squad leader, Dong, dispatched the original case handlers, escorted by Wang, to meet with the police officers from the Jiangjiabang Police Station of the North Station Precinct at Gaolangbu at 10 a.m. yesterday. They then apprehended another bandit, Jin Hengming, and took him into custody. After interrogation, Jin also confessed to robbing with Wang and, in October of last year, to robbing the Wanfeng Rice Shop at No. 750, the intersection of Xibaoxing Road and London Road in Zhabei, of more than 300 yuan in banknotes with his accomplices Zhao Xianglin, who was still at large, and two other unnamed individuals. He confessed to receiving a share of the stolen money. After the confession, the team dispatched detective Zhang Zhongliang, escorted by Wang, to the Mai Tian Silver Shop in Xiaodongmen yesterday morning to retrieve the original stolen gold ornaments. They also went to the Wanfeng Rice Shop on London Road to have Wang and Jin identified as the robbers. They then prepared a document and handed them over to the headquarters for processing.

Yesterday afternoon at around 1 p.m., at the intersection of Bailinan Road and Yuyuan Road in western Shanghai, Gu Huan (currently nine years old), the son of Gu Xu, a woman from Tongzhou who resides at No. 14, Fourteen Rooms, Caojiadu, was walking from south to north when a truck with municipal license plate No. 13422 sped towards him from the opposite direction. Qian Yonghai's Unfortunate Fate - Repeated Encounters with Thieves Lead to Thoughts of Ending It All 149

Qian Yonghai, a native of Qingpu, has been in the cloth business. A few years ago, he suffered significant losses due to customers owing him large sums of money, which led to the closure of his business. Qian has been unemployed and confined to his home for two years. He has asked friends and relatives to recommend him for business opportunities, and recently a relative introduced him to the Hengji Cotton Cloth Shop in Xinzha as a partner. Last month, the shop sent Qian to establish branches in the Qibao and Sijing areas in the interior to collect cloth. However, because the goods were not good and the purchase prices were very high, Qian closed the branches. As he was returning to Shanghai at the beginning of this month, he encountered bandits near Sijing. The bandits were furious when they found no silver dollars, so they stole Qian's account books, seals, and other items, and beat him up. Qian returned to Shanghai and reported the incident to the shop. The other day, the shop sent Qian again to Huangmiwu to set up a branch to collect goods and gave him 500 yuan in cash. Qian took the money and traveled by train the day before yesterday, getting off at Huangdu. After getting off and walking near Yang'e Pond, three bandits suddenly blocked his way and robbed him, stealing the 500 yuan in cash. After being robbed, he felt deeply resentful because he had been robbed twice and could not explain it to the shop. He immediately jumped into the pond to commit suicide. Fortunately, a small boat from Jiangbei rescued him. After questioning him, they sent Qian to Shanghai yesterday afternoon and accompanied him to the shop, where they informed them of Qian's encounters with the robberies and his attempted suicide. The shop then sent him to the hospital for treatment.

Glass Industry Association Submits a Letter 151

The Glass Industry Association sent a letter to the Customs Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, stating: "Respectfully, the members of our association, who are engaged in the glass business, all entrust foreign firms to order from overseas manufacturers, transport to Shanghai, and then sell to various ports in the country. According to regulations, they usually report for export with a permit. Even for scattered, non-boxed glass, they only need to present the permit to be exempted from export duties. However, your office has changed the old practice, requiring that all glass exports be in their original boxes; otherwise, an import tax must be paid upon arrival at the destination. It is understood that your office's new regulations are due to concerns about the potential for replacement and counterfeiting, as only the glass is affixed with paper-printed trademarks. Therefore, only original boxes are allowed, and the export of scattered, non-boxed glass is prohibited. The intention is good, and merchants should comply with it. However, glass products, unlike other items, have the difficulty of not being able to deeply engrave trademarks on the surface. As for ordinary glass of sizes 16 to 18, which are commonly priced at one hundred square feet per box, there are currently no difficulties in exporting them in their original boxes. However, large sheets, thick sheets, and patterned sheets contain hundreds of square feet per box, are more expensive, and have less demand, making it necessary to unpack or combine boxes for export. Since import duties have already been fully paid on glass imports, and there are no flat glass manufacturing plants in Shanghai or its neighboring areas, it can be known that all glass in Shanghai has already been taxed and there is no untaxed glass that can be used to offset the tax. Furthermore, glass is often broken during import, and if one wants to re-export it, the broken parts must be removed, making it impossible to keep the original box intact. Under the new regulations, this would also be subject to re-taxation. In this time of commercial recession, merchants cannot bear any additional burdens. Now that your office allows original boxes of glass to be exported tax-free, it seems that scattered, non-boxed glass should also enjoy the same treatment and should not be discriminated against, in order to achieve fairness. Therefore, we respectfully submit our difficulties and hope that your office will consider the merchants' difficulties and allow the old regulations to continue to be followed, so that scattered, non-boxed glass can be reported for export and be exempted from tax, just like original boxes. We respectfully request your consideration for the sake of public convenience."

Letter to the Editor 159

To the Esteemed Editor:

I am writing to you regarding the report in your newspaper's local news section about my residence being robbed and my abduction. I was shocked upon reading it. My residence was indeed robbed a month ago, and I promptly reported the loss to the Public Security Bureau and requested an investigation. The total loss was only about one hundred yuan. However, your newspaper reported that several thousand yuan were stolen. My family is not wealthy, so how could there be such a large sum of money? Exaggerating the facts is inconsistent with the truth. Furthermore, the report stated that I mistakenly associated with bandits and was held in soft custody for ransom. This is even more bizarre. While your newspaper claims to record everything that is heard and publish every manuscript, I was never abducted, and there was no ransom. Moreover, all my friends are well-behaved and there are no disreputable people among them. In addition, this news item is related to my personal reputation and financial well-being. Therefore, I am writing to you to clarify the truth and request that your newspaper promptly correct the previous erroneous report so that the outside world can understand the truth and there will be no further rumors. It would be a great service.

Sincerely,

Qian Sanduo

March 24th

Correspondence Address: Hata Temple, Huajingxiang, Erqu, Shanghai

Report on the Business of the Jin Cheng Bank in 1934 (12) 160

Table 1: Silver Imports and Exports in 1934 (in thousands of yuan)

Month Imported from Various Countries Exported to Various Countries Net Import or Export

August 354 79,449 79,095

September 820 48,960 48,140

October 607 56,939 56,332

November …… 9,070 9,070

December …… 2,310 2,410

Total 7,310 255,329 248,019

As silver flowed out, Shanghai's silver reserves naturally decreased. At the end of the year, the total reserves were only 33.5 million yuan, which was two-thirds of the mid-year total at the end of May, a decrease of 10.2 million yuan compared to the same period last year. However, the percentage of foreign banks in the silver reserves decreased monthly after starting at 49.2 percent at the beginning of the year, nearly half. It was only 17.7 percent in December, amounting to 5.6 million yuan. The percentage of Chinese banks was 82.3 percent, amounting to 26 million yuan. It can be seen that most of the silver outflow this year was exported by foreign banks. Only the total reserves decreased, which inevitably had an impact on the economic sector.

December 23,818 42,631 60,018 0.33 98.89

As silver flowed out and the amount of available currency in the market was insufficient, the amount of banknotes issued by banks increased accordingly. At the end of this year, the total amount of banknotes issued by various banks reached 41.1 million yuan, an increase of 6.6 million yuan or 19 percent compared to the end of 1933. In terms of the relative changes in issuance by different banks, the Central Bank had the fastest increase. Its issuance amount (accounting for 18.8 percent of the total) was second only to the Bank of China (accounting for 32.6 percent of the total). The total amount of reserves for the Four Banks, the China Industrial Bank, and the Commercial Bank also increased compared to the previous year. However, the China Bank, the Bank of Communications, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Ningbo Commercial Bank, and the Development Bank showed slight decreases.

This year's interbank lending rate was extremely low in the first six months because of the continuous influx of silver and Shanghai's abundant reserves, with the highest rate being no more than 9 percent and the lowest even being interest-free. It became slightly tighter in July. In August, as silver flowed out more, the interbank lending rate gradually increased, reaching a high of 15 percent and an average of 9 percent. In September, the United States announced the nationalization of silver, and silver prices soared, making interbank lending even more expensive, with a monthly average of 11.6 percent. After the export tax on silver, the outflow of silver slowed down slightly, and the interbank lending rate stabilized slightly. After November, due to supply and demand, the interbank lending rate increased again, reaching a high of 60 percent and a low of 20 percent, a rare record since the beginning of the year. However, the impact of last year's changes in the interbank lending rate on industry and commerce was minimal, as the fluctuations were entirely driven by the flow of silver and had little to do with commercial reasons. (To be continued)

Sports News

Fifteen Thousand People Become Manic: China Wins the Nations Cup. In the First Half, China's Performance Falters, Portugal Leads 1-0; The Result is a Thrilling 3-2 161

Yesterday, in an extremely chaotic and unfavorable situation, the Chinese football team almost lost to Portugal. Fortunately, they slightly improved in the second half and defeated the Portuguese team 3-2, winning the Nations Cup, which they had already given up for three years. The chaotic state of the Chinese formation in the first half was unprecedented. The forwards and inner defenders were flustered, and their ball skills were poor, leaving them helpless. Instead, the Portuguese team scored a goal. Within the first quarter of the second half, there was still no improvement. Li Yichen missed a penalty kick, leaving the audience in indescribable anxiety. After the Portuguese goalkeeper made a mistake and conceded a goal, the situation for China improved slightly. Subsequently, Li Yichen and Sun Jinshun each scored a goal. Finally, Portugal scored a penalty kick, resulting in a 3-2 score. Although the situation was very tense, there were very few exciting plays. Portugal was strong, with a fairly balanced attack and defense, only their goalkeeper was weak, and their left wing was slightly inferior. Colaça and Costa were steady and experienced as ever. In the first half, the performance of each Chinese player was unremarkable. Although Sun Jinshun worked hard, he achieved nothing. It was only after the first quarter of the second half that he entered a suitable state and was able to win. The stands around Shen Garden were packed with people, and the open space in front of the seats was also filled. Latecomers had no place to stand and rushed into the field, sitting around the outer perimeter, totaling more than fifteen thousand people, marking the first major event of this year's football season. Seeing the abnormal performance of the Chinese players in the first half, complaints were endless, like ants on a hot pot, extremely anxious. When the final victory was achieved, after the president of the Western Union, Grimshaw, presented the Nations Cup to the Chinese team captain, Li Ning, the ecstatic and frantic state was beyond description. The starting lineups of the two teams were as follows:

Chinese Team

Xu Heng

Li Ning Jiang Shanqing

Gu Shangrang Feng Yunyou Liang Shutang

Wan Xianghua Li Yichen Dai Linjing Sun Jinshun Jia Youliang

Portuguese Team

Su Chai

Ma Shan'er Victor

Remedy Costa F. Nata

C. Gonçalves L. Gonçalves Colaça Favão A. Nata

The Chaotic State is Frightening

Portugal kicked off first, but their probing attack was ineffective. Gu Shangrang passed the ball forward, but Wan Xianghua's cross was off target. The entire Portuguese army invaded the Chinese team's penalty area, charging left and right, which was frightening. The Chinese inner defenders felt unfamiliar, flustered, and unable to coordinate. The Portuguese right winger, Nata, missed two opportunities. Favão, full of ambition, broke through two defenses and passed to Colaça. Colaça charged towards the goal, but fortunately Xu Ting was alert and rushed out to block him. He also awarded Colaça a free kick, allowing them to escape danger. Costa returned with renewed vigor, and the Portuguese army surrounded them, making the area in front of the Chinese goal very dangerous. Fortunately, Jiang Shanqing defended effectively, preventing any accidents. Jia Youliang received a pass from center forward Dai, sending the ball into enemy territory. The goalkeeper panicked, giving China two corner kick opportunities, but they failed to score. The Portuguese attack was very strong, especially Colaça, who was frightening. Amidst the extremely bleak defense, China was fortunate enough to survive.

Chinese Team Captain Li Ning Holds the Nations Cup (Photo by Zhu Shunlin)

Poor Luck, Nothing Can Be Done

The Chinese forwards, like the inner defenders, were disorganized and listless, merely making lonely struggles, toiling back and forth, achieving nothing. Sun Jinshun once charged in but shot wide. Yi Chen attacked, but the ball grazed the right side of the goal. Jia Youliang rushed up and kicked, and the ball went into the goal with a bang. However, the referee blew the whistle and ruled it offside. After the Chinese team's frustration, Sun Jinshun went in again, intercepted the ball next to Remedy's feet, and rushed to the front of the goal, sweeping it away with force. Unexpectedly, it went straight at the goalkeeper, who calmly saved it. Once again, Old Sun sent the ball to the front of the goal, but Dai Linjing failed to reach it. Several opportunities were missed, and there was nothing that could be done about the poor luck.

The Loss of One Goal Leaves Everyone Stunned

Li Yichen shot again, but although the position was good, his foot was not accurate, and he could only sigh in frustration. Portugal's luck turned, and Nata launched an uprising on the border, copying to the Chinese hinterland. Gu Shangrang could not stop him, and he sent the ball in front of the goal. Jiang Shanqing closely guarded the goal, and the ball fell fifteen yards from the side of the battle. Gonçalves was unguarded and calmly shot, scoring. The entire audience was stunned, and the Chinese players were also panicked and tried to cheer up, but felt even more disorganized and helpless. The center defenders therefore did not dare to go forward, and were trapped at home. The forwards were even more lonely, only giving the opponent opportunities. China was thus trapped in a state of siege. Although the forwards had shots, they all missed. Fortunately, the first half was over, allowing them to rest and regroup.

The Penalty Kick is Missed

After quenching their thirst, the Chinese situation improved slightly, but was still unsatisfactory. Sun Jinshun received the ball from Little Wan, charged into an unguarded area, only seven or eight yards from the goal. He thought he could easily succeed, but little did he know that he was too hasty and missed again. Sighs arose from all around. Linjing, with the ambition of ten thousand men, was unwilling to yield and charged to the front of the goal, getting a chance for a penalty kick. The spectators felt like they had taken a cooling medicine, and that their wish could be fulfilled. Li Yichen stepped forward and kicked the ground towards the corner of the goal, but it went wide. Complaints did not cease. The bad luck had reached this point. The anxiety of the audience and players was indescribable.

From Despair to Triumph, Two Goals in a Row

At fifteen minutes, Gu Shangrang threw the ball in from the boundary line to Li Yichen. Li smoothly passed it to the front of the goal. The Portuguese goalkeeper caught it, took a step, and was about to kick it out, but unexpectedly his hand loosened and the ball fell to the ground. As if by divine intervention, the ball rolled into the goal behind him. Dai Linjing rushed to the front of the goal and kicked it hard, venting the anger in his chest. The spectators were overjoyed, and the repressed resentment was finally relieved. The sound of firecrackers arose from all around. From then on, the Chinese momentum greatly increased, and their spirits were high, washing away the previous disorganization and listlessness. The front and rear coordinated and communicated effectively. The opponent's goalkeeper was originally mediocre, and was panicked by the situation. Once, when a ball went out of bounds, he went to catch it, resulting in a corner kick. Little Wan sent it in very well, and Yichen headed it in from the front of the goal, very clearly. China then turned worry into joy and turned defeat into victory. The audience felt as if they had found a treasure, going manic and crazy.

Continuing Efforts Bring Another Success

At this point, the Portuguese lineup was slightly disordered. Furthermore, Ma Shan'er injured his foot and was reassigned to left inner forward, with Remedy being recalled. Left inner forward Gonçalves filled Remedy's vacancy, focusing on defense. China was thriving, and the Portuguese formation was thus disintegrated. In front of the goal, there were densely packed Chinese players, just like the Portuguese army had trapped China in the first half. Wan Xianghua received the ball from Yichen and shot towards the goal. The ball bounced back off the body of the enemy inner defender, Victor. Old Sun rushed forward and stole it, exercising his iron legs and shooting fiercely at the goal. The ball flew into the goal in a beautiful arc. China then took a very advantageous position of 3-1. From then on, there was no doubt that we would recover our lost territory.

Conceding a Penalty, But the Situation is Saved

With only a quarter of an hour left, both sides seemed exhausted but still fought hard without loosening up. Dai got the ball from Sun and charged under the goal. He could have taken the opportunity to shoot early, but he wanted to force his way into the goal and was overtaken by Remedy and tackled out. The goalkeeper then saved the ball and cleared it. The entire Portuguese army invaded, in a desperate attempt to succeed or die trying. Li Ning tried to steal the ball from Favão but was penalized with a penalty kick, which Costa took and swept in, making it 3-2. The Portuguese army continued to attack fiercely, trying to recover lost ground. Colaça and Favão both had frightening shots, but fortunately they missed. China then won 3-2, regaining the Nations Cup.

The Shanghai Secondary School Sports Federation, accepting the request of eight schools, including Chizhi, Minli, Aiguo, Shangzhong, Fuzhong, Numinli, Daxia, and Hujiang, held a provisional general meeting at the National Sports Association of China in Shen Garden at 10:00 AM yesterday, convened by the president. The members present were Sun Yiguang from Aiguo, Zhou Junren from Chizhi, Shen Kunnan from Minli, Xia Huanxin from Numinli, Han Yongkui from Fuzhong, Wang Huaiying from Daxia, Chen Bingde from Fushi (also representing Chongde), Lu Xiangqian from Guanghua, and Xu Zheng from Pudong, a total of ten school representatives. Lu Xiangqian chaired the meeting, and Sun Yiguang took the minutes. The proposals of each school and the resolutions of each case are recorded below.

(1) Chizhi representative proposed that the men's basketball competition should start, but several schools are still on spring break. Should the start be postponed for a few days? Resolved: The date of the men's basketball competition is changed to April 15.

(2) Chizhi and Fushi representatives proposed to amend the previous standing committee resolution regarding the restrictions on the qualifications of athletes. Athletes who have scored points in the National Games should not formally participate in the association's track and field competitions, and should only participate in an exhibition nature. The proposal was reconsidered and resolved: The previous proposal was overturned, and athletes who have scored points in the National Games may participate in various competitions organized by the association without restriction (passed by nine votes).

(3) Shanghai Private Middle School requested to join the association. Resolved: After investigation and report by the review committee, the qualifications for membership are met, and Shanghai Private Middle School is approved as a new member of the association (passed by nine votes).
