Educational News

National Higher Education Trends Since the Founding of the Republic 178

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics on the general state of national higher education for the 21st year of the Republic, which was reported in the newspapers. Now, we have sorted and summarized the already compiled national higher education situation over the years, recording the trends in national higher education since the founding of the Republic, and made some comparisons as follows:

(1) Number of Schools

The total number of higher education institutions nationwide in the 21st year of the Republic was 104 (76 universities and independent colleges, both public and private, and 28 specialized schools, both public and private). There were 103 in the 20th year, 86 in the 19th year, 70-plus in both the 17th and 18th years, 108 in the 14th year, and 80-plus in the 9th, 7th, and 5th years of the Republic. There were 104 schools in the 4th year and 102 in the 3rd year, 116 in the 2nd year, and 115 in the 1st year. Comparing these figures, the number of schools in the 1st and 2nd years of the Republic was actually higher than in the 21st year. However, the higher numbers at that time were mainly specialized schools. There were fewer universities. In the first year of the Republic, there were 111 private specialized schools and only 4 public and private universities and independent colleges. In the second year, there were 109 specialized schools and only 7 universities and independent colleges. In the third year, there were also 7 universities and independent colleges. From the fourth to the eighth years, there were 10 universities and independent colleges each year, and 11 in the ninth year. In the tenth year of the Republic, the number of universities and independent colleges increased to 15, 18 in the eleventh year, 24 in the twelfth year, 32 in the thirteenth year, and since the sixteenth year, the number has increased every year (44 schools in the 16th year, 49 in the 17th year, 50 in the 18th year, 59 in the 19th year, 73 in the 20th year, and 76 in the 21st year). From this, it can be seen that the increase in the total number of schools from the 1st to the 14th years of the Republic was mainly due to the increase in the number of specialized schools (the highest number of specialized schools was 111 in the 1st year, and the lowest was 58 in the 14th year). From the 17th to the 21st years of the Republic, the trend in higher education was a decrease in the number of specialized schools (from 25 to a maximum of 30) and an increase in the number of universities and independent colleges.

(2) Number of Teachers

The total number of teachers in higher education institutions nationwide in the 21st year of the Republic was 6,709 (5,974 in universities and 735 in specialized schools), 7,053 in the 20th year, 6,000-plus in both the 18th and 19th years, and 5,000-plus in the 17th year. From the 1st to the 5th years of the Republic, there were 2,000-plus teachers (including 1,000-plus teachers in specialized schools in the 3rd, 5th, 8th, and 9th years of the Republic). From the 17th to the 21st years of the Republic, the number of teachers in specialized schools ranged from 600-plus to 800-plus.

(3) Number of Students

The total number of "enrolled" university and specialized school students in the 21st year of the Republic was 42,710 (35,640 in universities and 7,070 in specialized schools), 44,167 in the 20th year, 37,566 in the 19th year, 29,123 in the 18th year, 25,198 in the 17th year, 36,321 in the 14th year, 17,241 in the 5th year, 25,242 in the 4th year, 33,373 in the 2nd year, and 42,114 in the 1st year. The number of "graduated" university and specialized school students was 7,311 in the 21st year, 7,034 in the 20th year, 4,000-plus in both the 19th and 18th years, 3,253 in the 17th year, 2,000-plus from the 12th to the 16th years, 1,000-plus from the 3rd to the 11th years, 976 in the 2nd year, and 490 in the 1st year.

(4) Amount of Funding

The total amount of funding in the 21st year was 33,203,821 yuan (31,625,252 yuan for universities and 1,887,569 yuan for specialized schools), 36,192,377 yuan in the 20th year (31,682,507 yuan for universities and 1,936,730 yuan for specialized schools), 29,867,474 yuan in the 19th year, 25,533,343 yuan in the 18th year, 17,909,810 yuan in the 17th year, 15,446,338 yuan in the 14th year, 3,673,155 yuan in the 5th year (883,069 yuan for universities and 2,790,086 yuan for specialized schools), 4,682,963 yuan in the 4th year (1,306,058 yuan for universities and 3,376,905 yuan for specialized schools), 5,728,476 yuan in the 3rd year (2,426,911 yuan for universities and 3,301,565 yuan for specialized schools), 4,171,372 yuan in the 2nd year (822,865 yuan for universities and 3,348,507 yuan for specialized schools), and 3,971,361 yuan in the 1st year (755,730 yuan for universities and 3,215,631 yuan for specialized schools). Comparing these figures, the funding for specialized schools from the 1st to the 14th years of the Republic was mostly around 3,000,000-plus yuan (also 2,700,000-plus in the 5th and 9th years). From the 17th year onwards, the funding for specialized schools decreased to 1,100,000-plus yuan, with a maximum of only 1,900,000-plus yuan. The funding for universities before the 14th year of the Republic was mostly no more than 2,400,000-plus yuan, with a minimum of only 700,000-800,000 yuan in the 1st and 5th years, which is forty times less than the recent 30,000,000-plus yuan.

Polish Naval School Ship to Arrive in Shanghai Around the 27th 183

The Dar Pomorza, a school ship of the Polish Naval Academy used by the Polish government to train merchant marine personnel, is scheduled to leave Nagasaki on the 24th of this month as part of a round-the-world voyage. Jiang Baili Expresses His Thoughts on the "Ten Declarations": Separation of Political Power, Military Force, and Knowledge Is the Source of Poverty and Weakness; Combination of Political Power, Military Force, and Knowledge Is the Foundation of Prosperity and Strength; Intellectuals Should Be Responsible and Practical in Their Work 184

Mr. Jiang Baili, who has been residing in Shanghai, has been deeply immersed in the study of Chinese cultural history in recent years and has gained significant insights. Yesterday, ten professors, signing themselves as the "Ten Declarations," jointly visited Mr. Jiang at his elegant studio. Mr. Jiang was in high spirits and full of wit and humor, still retaining his leisurely and graceful demeanor. Mr. Jiang first warmly treated the professors with delicacies and fine wine. As the wine flowed freely and the atmosphere became more relaxed, he delivered a long speech, which was deeply meaningful and highly valuable for young people across the country. A detailed record of his speech is provided below:

The morale of the nation has declined to such a state that if we do not point out a real path and a magic weapon, who will still believe? Idealism? Eastern culture? The Chan Buddhist nature and the Song Confucian principles were transplanted to the East to cultivate the so-called Bushido, but the producing country, China, has failed in every battle. Materialism? Western culture? Watt's machines and Edison's electricity are used by others to build wealth and enhance national power, to construct so-called capitalism. Fifty years ago, Japan was also once a colony, but China, which imported Western culture even earlier than Japan, has seen its rural areas declare bankruptcy and its factories demand relief. Is it because people are incurable and all medicines are ineffective? If so, the name "Chinese flag" should have disappeared centuries ago. Why is it that even today, there is still a large population living on the mainland? Let us examine the past and find out what the real skills of the Chinese flag are.

From the rise and fall of the Chinese flag, from the beginning of world history to the present day, I have discovered a fundamental principle: "Those whose living conditions are consistent with their combat conditions are strong; those whose conditions are separate are weak; and those whose conditions are opposite perish." Living and combat are essentially the same thing seen from two different perspectives. However, based on the evolution of economic and combat conditions, there is a tendency for separation at all times. Although Greece and Rome have earned the reputation of being culturally advanced in Europe, the inheritors of Greek and Roman culture today are not the Greeks and Romans of that time. The general reason for their great culture and eventual decline is the inconsistency between their living tools and their combat tools.

There are two types of consistency between living conditions and combat conditions that have been unconsciously achieved through natural tools. One is the Mongols' horse, and the other is the British's ship. They used horses to find water and grass and used ships to conduct business. Horses and ships were both tools for eating and tools for fighting. Therefore, they conquered the world twice. There are also two types that have been successfully achieved through elaborate artificial systems. One is the Westerners' national mobilization, which was invented during World War I and implemented only in the last ten years, and the other is the well-field system and feudalism that China implemented 3,000 years ago. Its true spirit is the consistency between living conditions and combat conditions.

Feudalism is not tribal separatism (recent people who refer to separatist tribal ideology as feudal ideology are using the term incorrectly). It is a tool to break tribal separatism. Conferment is colonization, and construction is a consistent construction of living (economy) and combat (national defense). The well-field system is not about equal distribution of property (which was not a strange thing at the time). It is a national defense system that allows people to farm and eat while also being able to send troops to fight (which was national mobilization at the time). Zhou Gong was the one who understood and created this principle. Guan Zhong was the one who inherited it (the Zuo Zhuan says that the territory of Qi, "exhausted its fields to the east," which proves the relationship between the field system and the military system). Shang Yang was the one who finally succeeded. This is the real skill of the Chinese nation that I have discovered. If you can systematically describe it so that young people can feel the greatness of the inherent skills of our Chinese nation, that we were able to unify the Asian continent in the past, why can't we unify the world in the future? Perhaps it will provide some remedy for the current decline in morale. (To be continued)

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 185

— (Master of Shiyuan)

Every store has a stream of people browsing, but the coffin shop is the most deserted; however, the most reliable and profitable business is still the coffin shop. No matter how depressed the world is, the coffin shop seems to be immune. Moreover, the more panicked society is, the more depressed all industries are, the more miserable people's lives are, and the less secure people's lives are, the better the coffin shop's business is.

The most frightening thing to pass by is the coffin shop, the most frightening thing to encounter is a coffin procession, and the most unbearable thing is a three-inch paulownia coffin with a corpse lying horizontally. People are arrogant and invincible in life, but they cannot escape this tragic and desolate ending, which is the most unclean and unpleasant moment. There are countless birds flying in the sky, but after death, they are invisible and traceless, clean and tidy. Can humans not be as good as birds?!

Work and reward are, in fact, completely opposite. A university professor can effortlessly receive tens of dollars for teaching one hour; an elementary school teacher shouts all day long, working as an assistant and even doing chores, and still cannot earn more than tens of dollars a month. A small clerk in an agency, careful and diligent, busy and dizzy, extremely hard-working, earns only tens of dollars a month. A high-ranking official, sitting in a high position, bored and idle, receives a salary that is not counted, and public expenses are also one hundred, two hundred, ... dollars.

Random Notes on Nanchang 186

— Shu

Since the relocation of the military headquarters to Hongdu, officials and dignitaries have gathered, and hotels and civilian houses have been rented out completely. Rental prices have skyrocketed, and landlords have all profited threefold. Later arrivals cannot obtain even a tiny piece of land for tens of gold. Recently, with the relocation of the military headquarters to Han, officials and their families have departed one after another, and many empty houses have suddenly become available. The "for rent" signs, which were never seen before, have gradually increased. Landlords are unwilling to lower prices for the time being, still demanding the original rent, resulting in many houses remaining unoccupied. Moreover, many newly built hotels and civilian houses are still under construction, leaving the owners in a dilemma.

Residents have deep-rooted habits, and although they have undergone the baptism of the New Life Movement, it seems that they have not been fundamentally reformed. During the Lunar New Year, firecrackers are set off in every household, lasting for more than ten days. Recent temple fairs in the suburbs and lantern festivals in the city still follow the old customs. Middle and lower-class families still use rickshaws for wedding processions, with a red silk bundle tied on top. The use of automobiles is limited to incumbent high-ranking officials, as commercial automobile companies are rare, and most of the households relocated from bandit areas are poor. Few local residents are from wealthy families.

Newspapers from Shanghai arrive here in four days at the earliest, and magazines published half a month ago are still not seen for sale. There are more than ten bookstores, most of which sell discounted books and magazines as their main business. Specialized works have limited sales, and Western books, except for the Commerce, China, and World Publishing Houses, are not sold in other stores.

There are seven or eight daily newspapers, with mediocre editing and printing. In the past, the main source of material was news about bandit suppression. Now that the military campaign to suppress bandits has ended, the source of manuscripts is quite lacking, and editors are all frowning.

Armored Car 187

— Yun Sun

"Armored Car" is Mr. Hu's nickname, but when we see these three characters, our blood vessels burst and we experience waves of hidden pain! Mr. Hu has this nickname, which seems quite fun on the surface, alas! It's very sad, it only started after January 28th: we haven't seen the scars given by the armored car, so its power is not obvious. Maybe many people couldn't call out this name before this weapon of war; Mr. Hu is an athlete, he is the first graduate of the gymnastics school in the late Qing Dynasty, he is fifty-five years old this year, he has lived in Shanghai for decades, he never relies on vehicles when walking alone, he participates in amateur race walking competitions every time, and he runs like a charge even when he takes a casual walk, the leather shoes he wears are different from ordinary styles, the sound is clattering, like an armored car chasing; he has statistics on wearing leather shoes, a total of one hundred and twenty-five pairs; he is good at steel-pen drawings, willow branch writing, and he also drew a fan for this journal's "Du Weng" the year before last; he is good at photography, he knows music, he is a versatile athlete, and he still works as a physical education teacher; every thread on his body is different from ordinary people, a pair of narrow-rimmed gold-rimmed glasses from the newest style, changed to the oldest style, from the oldest style, and changed to today's most modern; he is a free love, his wife is a female student who he successfully chased during his school days, he held a civilized wedding, and was the original sixth in Shanghai; he goes to sleep, and gets up as soon as he wakes up, and doesn't sleep again, saying that sleeping again is like an extra, enough is enough, he doesn't need it; so no matter the cold, heat, warmth, he always gets up at four o'clock, he walks from Fang Xie Road in Ximen to the Shanghai-Taizhou bus station in Zhabei, takes a turn, and it's still eight o'clock in the morning; his umbrella, the upper part goes to the top pole, the lower part goes to the handle pole, only the area of the umbrella cloth, rolled into a layer of newspaper, is held under his arm, light and exquisite, shielding from the sun on sunny days, acting as rain on rainy days; everything else is very unique; so the students also call him "Civilized Mr."

Decorations from the Seabed 188

— Zuo

Digging Ditches and Other Matters 189

— Du Yun

In Shanghai, there are several special occupations that are not seen in the inland areas, "digging ditches" being one of them. Because the ditches on the side of the road are set up to hold rainwater, there will be passers-by in normal times who inadvertently drop coins, ornaments, and so on. Or the loss is limited and not worth retrieving; or when it is lost, even the person himself did not realize it, so there is a kind of person who "digs ditches" to earn a living!

The drainage holes on both sides of the road are deeper! The "ditch digger" has to have one device to make a support and be able to move around. One hand holds a bamboo pole, the head of the pole is tied with a scoop, first move the drainage hole cover, insert the bamboo pole as much as possible, scoop to the bottom, drag the mud and water, and pour it on the side of the hole; another quick hand gropes and picks out copper coins, silver corners, etc., and throws them into a jar. The hand section must be agile, and the eyes must be sharp. Digging one hole after another, calmly, two people can earn more than half a dollar a day on average.

The drainage ditches in the alleys are shallower! Just one person, rolling up their sleeves and reaching in to grope inside. According to their experience, the area around Shantou Road Xiaohuayuan Daqingli is a lucrative place. Once every half month, each hole can have eighty or ninety copper coins, because people in brothels often welcome and send people at midnight, and copper coins and silver corners are often dropped in the dark and slip into the drain.

"Digging drainage ditches" is already a special occupation, but there are also those who rely on sweeping garbage and brushing dust to make a living. It is said that in silver shops, someone is willing to pay hundreds of dollars a year to take over the garbage and dust, not only sweeping the ground clean every day, but also wiping the dust on the walls and the dirt on the tables; even the old clothes worn by silversmiths and the old shoes worn on their feet are willing to give you new ones in exchange for your old ones. Because in silver shops, gold and silver scraps are scattered everywhere, they will use all methods to collect them, make something out of nothing, and the profits are still very high!

Little Western Paradise 190

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 11: Melancholy Night Talk: A Life is But a Dream; Scattered Footprints: The Wind and Rain Are Too Oppressive

Jia Duocai said, "It's very late. Xi'an city is pitch black, you can't see where you're going. Take this flashlight with you." Yang Huanhua smiled, revealing her teeth, and said, "I don't need to go, I've already paid for the room next door. I'm not leaving until tomorrow morning." As she spoke, she steadied herself by holding onto the edge of the table, as if hesitating. Seeing that Jia Duocai didn't say anything, she finally said, "Mr. Jia, I'm intruding on you tonight." After saying that, she smiled slightly again. Seeing that Jia Duocai still didn't say anything, she lowered her head and left. Jia Duocai didn't move either. He composed himself and smoked two cigarettes. In his heart, he thought about how there were all kinds of people in this Little Western Paradise hotel. Two large gasoline lamps were lit at the entrance. Old-fashioned horse-drawn carriages, ordinary rickshaws, and automobiles from big cities were all parked haphazardly, creating a lively scene. The poor people passing by the entrance all wondered how they could get inside. But they didn't realize that among the people staying here, there were those who were comfortable, but there were even more who were not as well off as the poor people outside who couldn't get in. Take Zhang Jiewei, for example, he fancied himself as a young master. Just because I promised to write a letter to Director Gao, he eagerly took on the task of pimping. Thinking about him, he's probably not unlike this Miss Yang, feeling very uncomfortable inside. Alas! It's hard to make a living. That was what he was thinking in his heart, and unconsciously, he sighed out the word "alas." He was leaning back in his chair, smoking, not paying attention to anything outside himself. At this moment, a quiet voice said, "Mr. Jia, are you feeling very sad?" Jia Duocai immediately sat up straight and looked around, but there was no one there. Just as he was feeling very strange, the small voice said again, "Mr. Jia, I'm peeking at you through the crack in the wall. Would you like to come and sit with me?" Jia Duocai then realized that Yang Huanhua was still there, spying on him. He nodded towards the wall and said, "No need, I'm going to sleep." (165)

Records of Royal Fragrance,缥缈 191

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

The Empress Dowager, in order to show me a realistic example, took me to the silkworm room to observe. In several small bamboo trays, I indeed saw many silkworm moths; although they had wings, they could not fly, but could only crawl clumsily forever.

These moths were also divided into male and female, and they were mixed together in a bamboo tray. This bamboo tray was their world; apart from this bamboo tray, they could not touch anything else. And they themselves seemed to have no ambition to think about going outside the bamboo tray; as for how big the content of this bamboo tray was, or whether it was safe for them, they didn't care at all. What's even stranger is that unlike other insects, after they turned into moths, they didn't want to eat anything; their activity was just to choose a mate and mate with each other. After mating once, the male died first, leaving only the females to complete the task of laying eggs. At this time, the silkworm-raising girls had to pick out the dead male moths and discard them, so as not to obstruct. Underneath the bamboo tray, white paper had been laid out long ago. After a day or two, the female moths would lay their eggs on the paper. When I looked again the next night, I saw countless silkworm eggs, like black sesame seeds, scattered on the paper, and many dead female moths. Of course, they were no longer needed and were immediately discarded.

"Don't you find it very interesting? Really! This is nothing less than a microcosm of life!" The Empress Dowager said in a philosophical tone, "From birth, they hurriedly complete the work they should do in their life, and then die very quickly. There is only a short period of ten or twenty days in between. But these ten or twenty days are the same for them as for us, from crawling out of our mother's womb, from infancy to childhood, from childhood to adulthood, from adulthood to middle age, old age, and finally death. There is really no difference!" (276)

Profiles

Shanghai Daotai in Modern History 192

— Shanghai News Agency

Flipping through history books, we found that many important figures in the officialdom used to be Shanghai Daotais: not to mention the complete history of the Qing Dynasty, just in modern history, there are these few:

(1) Lü Haihuan: He was appointed as the Shanghai Daotai in the 22nd year of Guangxu, but by the 29th year of Guangxu, he was already the Minister of Commerce and Trade of the Qing government. At that time, the Shanghai revolutionary movement was just beginning, and he immediately sent a letter to Su Fuen Shou, informing him that "There are so-called enthusiastic young people in the Shanghai concession who are gathering in Zhang Garden to discuss matters, nominally to reject France and Russia, but in reality, they are trying to rebel." He immediately named Cai Yuanpei, Wu Jingheng, Zhang Binglin, and Niu Yongjian for investigation and arrest. Although it was not permitted by the Bureau of Works, it later caused the sensational Su Bao case.

(2) Cai Jun: He was appointed as the Shanghai Daotai in the 23rd year of Guangxu, but by the 28th year of Guangxu, he was already the Qing government's ambassador to Japan. At that time, in order to promote racial revolution and revive historical concepts, Zhang Binglin and others initiated the "242nd Anniversary Commemoration of the Fall of China" in Tokyo, which shocked the Japanese academic community. He was extremely panicked and personally visited the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting that the association be disbanded. The Japanese government granted his request, and a large number of students studying abroad were forced to return to China. In Shanghai, the Patriotic Society was established and the China Public School was founded.

(3) Rui Cheng: He was appointed as the Shanghai Daotai in the 32nd year of Guangxu, but by the time of the Wuchang Uprising of the Xinhai Revolution, he was already the Governor-General of Huguang. At that time, he first received a secret telegram from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Qing government, which briefly stated: "The revolutionary party Huang Xing has scheduled an uprising." Therefore, he conducted strict investigations and defenses, and captured several party members. He thought that the revolutionary organization had been broken and there would be no major trouble, and he was quite pleased with himself. Wuchang had 16,000 new troops, divided into infantry, cavalry, and artillery. They usually harbored resentment, and at this time, Rui Cheng arbitrarily searched and arrested them on suspicion. As a result, it was launched on the 19th day of the eighth month, and Rui abandoned the city and fled.

The above is a brief account of the important ones; the other minor ones are not listed.

Shen Bao Medical and Pharmaceutical Weekly

A History of Public Health Progress (II) 193

— A lecture by Zhu Jiqing, Director of the Health Education Department of the Health Department (Notes by Cheng Xinliang)

(1) Training of personnel. Training of a large number of medical and nursing staff in order to achieve a public medical system.

(2) Medical education. Educating medical and nursing talents with a positive medical concept.

(3) Public education. The education above alone is not enough. Medicine is not a secret treasure. It is not the private property of doctors. It is a public asset of mankind. Therefore, medicine is absolutely open and should be applied daily. We know that for thousands of years, medicine has been like a secret treasure, so mysterious that it cannot be explained. Especially in the last thirty years, so-called scientific medicine has regarded it as a family heirloom and a golden career. If anyone knew a little medicine and applied it, it would be like committing a capital crime. There is no doubt that this is human selfishness. But now we must overthrow them. We must eliminate them. Medicine must be made public from now on. It is no longer the magic weapon of a few people. From now on, everyone has the right to apply medicine. From now on, what doctors give us is not just needles and medicine, but a true gift that contains educational medicine. From now on, the health and survival of mankind are guaranteed. This is the value of medical items, and it is also the active period of medicine.

(5) The evolution of public health

We have a considerable understanding of the relationship between medicine and society, and the changes in concepts mentioned above. Now let's talk about the evolution of public health itself.

The words "public health" probably originated in the period when medicine began to focus on ill health. During this period, mankind felt that health was an absolute necessity, and that health was not just about taking medicine. There must be some kind of overall plan. Therefore, people gradually began to pay attention to the health aspect. We summarize it as public health.

The evolution of public health can be divided into four stages.

(1) Environmental health. This period probably began in the 18th century. In this century, bacteriology and disinfection were invented. (Pasteur invented bacteria, Lister invented disinfection) Other inventions, such as the progress of anatomy and physiology, and the invention of X-rays, emerged like bamboo shoots after a rain, showing their brilliance. Scientific authority, the glory of mankind

At this time, people knew that diseases were caused by a tiny and invisible microorganism, a bacterium. These microorganisms mostly exist in the environment around people. Therefore, the health experts at this time regarded environmental improvement as the primary task of health. Such as the improvement of tap water and other drinking water, the construction of sewers, the treatment of garbage, and the cleanliness of streets. This is the initial prototype of public health. Civilized and advanced countries such as England, France, and Switzerland all did these jobs at first.

(2) Disease prevention. This is something that has happened in the last seventy years. Medical scientists believe that environmental health is only part of public health. To protect human health, it is necessary to prevent the invasion of epidemics. Therefore, the widespread and bold use of vaccination, and various prophylactic vaccinations of active and passive vaccines and serums, such as diphtheria antitoxin typhoid vaccine. The invention of Scarlet Fever Serum—diseases caused by bacteria can be prevented by vaccination to achieve immunity or antitoxin. Other methods such as disinfection and isolation are also well applied.

Public health has made great progress.

(3) Early diagnosis and treatment. Even now, there are still many diseases that are not caused by bacteria, but by physiological and tissue changes. Such as cancer, tonsil swelling, and dental defects. These are all simple tissue changes. If diagnosed early and treated, cancer can be completely cured.

The evolution of public health is so amazing.

(4) Public education. I said above that medicine is like a daily necessity for the public. It is not the private property of a few doctors. Moreover, doctors cannot manage many things. I must declare that I am not looking down on doctors. Moreover, I especially admire doctors who are scientific and psychologically sound (truly moral). However, what I mean is that the knowledge and experience of medicine and disease prevention should be known and assisted in practice by everyone. I myself am also a doctor and dare not belittle myself. A naked heart is laid bare in front of everyone. There are no secrets. Everyone, look. This is medicine. This is the medicine of the human masses. Doctors are in a position of research and guidance. The public is in a position of experience.

Public health has evolved to this stage, which can be considered the peak.

(5) Preventive medicine. Public health, since it has progressed to the peak position with the power of society, we dare not say that it cannot be further improved. But we are actively doing it.

I said that reading history can teach you many experiences. We can turn these experiences into our own experiences. We can catch up head-on and take fewer detours.

At the same time, we can also know that the mortality rate of civilized and advanced Western countries is much lower than ours. The life expectancy is also much higher than ours. Therefore, they can make their countries rich and strong and increase their status. Looking back at our home, what is it like? Bending over and hunching shoulders, yellow face and thin muscles, high mortality and low life expectancy. How painful!

Therefore, the purpose of our future public health management is to:

Reduce mortality. Increase human lifespan. Improve health. Transform the nation. Enhance international status. (End)

Skin Hygiene and Prevention of Skin Diseases (IV) 194

— Xie Yunshou

Third is soap. When we wash, we often use soap. It is easy to remove dirt and other unclean things, so that the skin is completely clean. Therefore, soap is very important for skin hygiene. Therefore, its types and effects must be understood.

The ingredients of soap are made by mixing alkali salts (that is, sodium brine or potassium brine) and fat and boiling them. It is a chemical mixture that can be divided into two types: sodium soap and potassium soap. Sodium soap has a soft texture. Potassium soap has a hard texture. There is also a type that is made by fully mixing alkali and fat. This is called neutral soap. Its effect is the mildest.

Soap dissolves in water and can form foam. Applying it to the skin can not only dissolve the fat on the skin surface, but also make the stratum corneum of the skin expand and soften, making it easier to peel off. Therefore, the attached dust and dirt are also easily removed. The stronger the alkali of the soap, the stronger its effect. However, hard water is not suitable for the application of soap. If it must be used, it is best to boil it. At this time, soap is effective for cleaning the skin, but it should be moderate. If used excessively, it will be harmful to the skin. Because when the skin is thin and has little fat, excessive use of soap will strip away the sebum of the skin, making it lose its luster and become dry and rough, which can easily cause chapped skin and eczema. Therefore, people with thin skin and lack of sebum should not use too much soap. If you must use it, you should also choose a mild one. If it is also inappropriate, you can use rice bran juice instead. On the contrary, people with more sebum should use soap often. Even a slightly stronger one is not harmful. The nature of the skin also varies depending on the location. For example, the hair on the head is abundant, and there is also a lot of sebum. Strong potassium soap can be applied. The strength and weakness mentioned here refer to the nature and effect of soap. The most ideal soap is neutral sodium soap. It can be used often without harm. There are two conditions for choosing soap. First, when making soap, do not mix in various by-products. Second, there must be no free excessive alkali. If there is free alkali, it will irritate the skin and saltify the fat on the epidermis, making the skin rough. However, the determination of whether soap is good or bad is actually very difficult. It is best to try it yourself. If there are no unexpected irritations, dryness, roughness, tension, etc. on the skin after trying it, there will probably not be excessive alkali.

The above are commonly used soaps. There is also a type called medicated soap, which is the potassium soap mentioned above. Its alkali is very strong and is not suitable for ordinary use. It can only be used for medicinal purposes to remove large amounts of sebum, dust, and dandruff. The other medicated soaps mentioned contain various drugs. This is not suitable for ordinary skin hygiene and is used for special skin diseases.

The purpose of using medicated soap is to assist in local treatment of the skin. For example, acne, seborrhea, and parasitic diseases (tinea, ringworm, etc.). If you use it without asking about the symptoms, it will have various disadvantages. Also, merchants often have improper quality because of profit. At the same time, it is stored in the window for a long time. This is not only unsuitable for application, but also because the drug components are denatured and its volatile substances are dissipated, becoming ineffective. Therefore, it is best not to use such medicated soap.

Medicated soaps have many types due to the different properties of the drugs. For example, boric acid soap has the mildest properties. In addition, tar soap, sulfur soap, and "Nafta" soap can be used for seborrhea, acne, folliculitis, and parasitic skin diseases. Peppermint soap and carbolic acid soap can be used for pruritus and other itchy skin diseases. However, it should be prohibited during fresh acute symptoms. Ichthyol soap can be used for seborrhea, acne, and rosacea. Hebra's potassium soap essence (potassium soap and alcohol mixed in equal parts) can remove the dandruff and scalp oil on the head. It is most suitable for cleaning. Therefore, it is most suitable for people with a large amount of scalp oil (commonly known as dandruff). The medicated soaps mentioned above are used in the same way as ordinary soaps. Use hot water to wash and be sure to wash away the foam thoroughly.

When washing with ordinary soap, hot water is better than cold water. But at the same time, you should pay attention to the sensitivity of the skin. That is, the use of soap should be restrained for sensitive skin. Otherwise, the skin on the face may become rough. If washing with water makes the skin rough, add some borax (two teaspoons in half a basin of water) or boric acid (two teaspoons) to soften the irritation of the washing water (especially when it is hard water).

There is a kind of person who often adds some milk when washing their face. This is very suitable for sensitive and rough skin. (That is, add one part boiled milk to three parts of water) Because it uses the fat in the milk to cover the skin, it can avoid the irritation of water and has a protective effect.

It is best to avoid washing diseased skin. If you want to wash, you must also pay extreme attention. It must not be an irritating friction. And

Page 16

The washing time should be short. After wiping it dry, sprinkle it with powder to make it fully dry. Also, people with sensitive facial skin should not go outside immediately after washing to come into contact with outside air. Therefore, washing is best done at night. (End)

Current Situation of Medicine and Health in Songjiang 195

— Fu Jiren

(5) Physician Level

The qualifications of practicing physicians in Songjiang can be roughly divided into eight: (1) Graduates from Chiba Medical University in Japan. (2) Graduates from National Tongji University. (3) Graduates from the former Jiangsu Provincial Medical College. (4) Graduates from Shanghai Southeast Medical College. (5) Graduates from Zhejiang Provincial Medical and Pharmaceutical College. (6) Graduates from Hangzhou Guangji Medical School. (7) Nurses who have obtained a general physician license. (8) Those who open a business after practicing in various hospitals. Physicians have good moral concepts and no factional differences, but there are often advertisements that exaggerate private equipment, but the actual equipment is very lacking.

(6) Consultation Fees and Medicine Costs

(A) Consultation fees: Hospitals are divided into four categories: free consultation, outpatient consultation, special consultation, and house call. Free consultations are mostly ten copper coins. Outpatient consultations range from four small silver coins, four large silver coins, and half a large silver coin. Special consultations cost one large silver coin, and house calls cost two large silver coins. Overtime is doubled. Private clinics charge different fees. Some charge four small silver coins, and some charge half a silver coin. Some provide free consultations on Sundays or at certain times every day to benefit the poor.

(B) Medicine costs. Doctors in Songjiang all have their own pharmacies, because pharmacies do not dispense prescriptions. The fees vary greatly. For example, in county hospitals, foreign medicines are divided into three types of porcelain boxes: large, medium, and small, each with a certain amount. Internal medicines are based on the number of days of consumption. For example, if one day's amount is 30 cents of a large silver coin, then two days is 60 cents. The prices are not based on the price of the medicine, which is very ridiculous. Other hospitals or doctors charge differently. For example, injections cost two yuan each. Therefore, very few patients receive injections. The price for pigments and other similar substances ranges from three to four yuan. 914 costs about four to five yuan. If the medicine is purchased by oneself, the surgery fee ranges from one to two yuan.

(7) Obstetrics

There are three hospitals with obstetrics departments. One is Chonghua, one is Pingzheng, and one is the Maternity Hospital attached to Deqiong Hospital. Chonghua is the most famous and has a branch hospital. The dean is Sun Chonghua, a female physician and a graduate of Hangzhou Guangji School. She has rich knowledge and experience. She can be said to be the leading new medical obstetrician in Songjiang. This hospital has been open for a long time and is highly trusted by the people of Songjiang. There are seven practicing midwives in the city. The above-mentioned four hospitals all have obstetrics departments and employ one or two midwives.

The people of Songjiang are still able to trust the new medical obstetrics. The fees also vary from person to person, about four yuan, six yuan, eight yuan, and sometimes increase or decrease depending on the economic situation of the patient's family. Unfortunately, it cannot be fully popularized and is mostly limited to the intellectual class. There are fewer inpatients, unless it is a difficult birth. There is no public civilian maternity hospital in this county, which is a shortcoming!

(8) New Pharmacies

There are five new pharmacies in Songjiang: Nanyang, Jihuatang, Huamei, Sino-British, and Da Wuzhou. Nanyang specializes in the pharmaceutical business, and has more medicines than other stores. It also has a branch clinic with three doctors. The other four stores also sell cosmetics, especially Da Wuzhou Pharmacy, which is jointly established with a Chinese ginseng store. Chinese and Western medicines are displayed separately in the two display windows, which is interesting. At first glance, it is impossible to tell whether it is Chinese or Western. None of the stores has a formal pharmacist who can dispense prescriptions. I once went to each pharmacy to try to get a prescription dispensed, and saw that each store used apprentices to serve customers. Except for a few people, they were all apprentices who did not know or understand the original foreign names, and acted as salespersons for Western medicines. Isn't that a joke? Most of the medicines are domestic medicines that are cheap. There are many common medicines that cannot be bought in the early city, such as Licorice Juice (Sucus Liguiri Siae), Alum stick (Alaumstiift), and Ferric Chloride Solution (Liq Ferri Sesquichlorati), which makes me, a doctor who just arrived in Songjiang, unable to prescribe. There is really no place to complain. This journal once reported that disassembled injection drugs could be purchased in the pharmacies of Huaiyin County, and the same is true in Songjiang. Compared with the original packaging, the price may be one to two times higher. According to my investigation, this phenomenon is caused by unlicensed doctors in Songjiang who specialize in giving injections.

Common Sense Q&A about Diseases 196

— Cheng Hanzhang

(54) Beriberi (4)

(Question) What symptoms occur in the respiratory system of people with beriberi?

(Answer) Respiratory symptoms include difficulty breathing. The throat, bronchi, and lungs may experience mucositis, and pulmonary edema may also occur.

(Question) What happens within the digestive system?

(Answer) Symptoms in the stomach include fullness in the epigastric region, lack of appetite, and acid reflux with a burning sensation. During beriberi-related heart distress, symptoms such as thirst, nausea, and vomiting may arise. Within the intestines, constipation is a common symptom.

(Question) Do beriberi patients experience fever?

(Answer) Fever only occurs in acute, severe cases of beriberi, presenting as irregular and remitting, around 37 to 38 degrees Celsius. It disappears as the condition improves. If the fever exceeds 39 degrees, there is a risk of complications.

(Question) What is the typical duration of beriberi?

(Answer) Most cases of beriberi can be cured after several weeks to months. However, those who neglect self-care, such as overworking or having an unbalanced diet, are prone to recurrence or worsening of the condition.

(Question) What is the prognosis for beriberi? Is it good or bad?

(Answer) If treated promptly and thoroughly, even severe or cardiac beriberi can be completely cured. The mortality rate varies depending on the region, prevalence, and time of year. The causes of death are often complications, cardiac paralysis (cardiac beriberi), and paralysis of the respiratory muscles.

(Question) What are the key points in diagnosing this disease?

(Answer) The key points in diagnosing beriberi are: (1) Heaviness in the lower limbs; (2) Sensory abnormalities, especially numbness; (3) Edema; (4) Loss of Achilles or patellar tendon reflexes; (5) Cardiac symptoms, such as palpitations, rapid pulse, and enlarged heart sounds; (6) Tension in the calf muscles.

(Question) With which diseases should beriberi be differentiated?

(Answer) It should be differentiated from kidney diseases, valvular heart disease, spinal tuberculosis, myelitis, Landry's paralysis, toxic polyneuritis, acroesthesia, progressive muscular atrophy, and starvation edema.

(Question) How should we prevent beriberi?

(Answer) To prevent beriberi, first, improve the diet and eat more foods containing vitamin B1. Base your diet on wheat and unpolished rice, and consume plenty of fruits, beans, vegetables, fish, and meat. Second, pay attention to hygiene by avoiding dampness and excessive heat, and living in cooler, drier places. Third, avoid physical and mental exhaustion, and engage in moderate exercise.

(Question) What is the general outline of beriberi treatment?

(Answer) Treatment for beriberi should focus on rest, diet, medication, and relocation.

(Question) What are the effects of rest?

(Answer) Rest allows the patient's cardiac symptoms to improve. Severe cases, in particular, require absolute rest.

(Question) How should the patient's diet be selected?

(Answer) Focus on eating foods rich in vitamin B1, such as fresh vegetables (spinach, cauliflower), fruits (sweet potatoes, apples, oranges, grapes), beans (soybeans, broad beans), milk, eggs, fresh fish and meat.

(Question) What medications should be used?

(Answer) Use large doses of vitamin B1 preparations, administered orally or by injection. Diuretics, mild laxatives, and cardiac tonics may also be used.

(Question) What is the method of treatment through relocation?

(Answer) Move the patient to the countryside, especially to a highland area. Pay attention to the patient's heart strength during this time. Gradual recovery of health is possible. (End)

Medical Knowledge for Pain Relief (7) 197

— Li Xing

Stomach Pain

Cooked meats and broths should always be lightly seasoned and well-cooked. Avoid coarse greens (high-fiber vegetables) and spicy or sour ingredients, as well as strong seasonings. Strive to provide ample nourishment to increase the patient's health and resistance, so that the stomach pain ceases and the stomach ulcer can fully heal.

The most important medications for stopping stomach ulcer pain are alkaline and antacid substances. We know that stomach acid causes stomach ulcer pain, but stomach acid is essential for digestion. Using alkaline and antacid medications neutralizes the stomach acid. This prevents the stomach acid from irritating the stomach ulcer, thereby stopping the pain. This method removes the stimulus from the nerve receptors at the site of the stomach ulcer; it does not anesthetize the stomach ulcer, nor does it anesthetize the brain. This is a beneficial and harmless method of stopping stomach pain. From this, it is even clearer that the practice of simply anesthetizing the brain with opium or morphine is a deceptive method of pain relief. Understanding this basic principle, I believe that rational citizens will never choose narcotics to deceive and harm themselves. Those who have not been fooled by addictive drugs should avoid trying them, and those who have already been fooled should quickly give them up and adopt scientific methods of pain relief when experiencing stomach pain. This is what is meant by, "The sea of suffering is boundless; turn your head and the shore is at hand."

The most effective alkaline and antacid medications are bismuth subcarbonate, magnesium oxide, calcium carbonate, and baking soda. The effectiveness of these medications varies in duration, so it is best to take them in combination. Belladonna and other medications are also beneficial for stomach pain, depending on whether they are taken appropriately.

Perforation of a Stomach Ulcer A perforated stomach ulcer means that the ulcer has created a hole, connecting the inside of the stomach to the abdominal cavity. Fluids from the stomach can then flow into the abdominal cavity. This is a very serious condition. Why? Because stomach fluids entering the abdominal cavity will cause peritonitis. This type of peritonitis is extremely dangerous. If not treated properly, it is truly a case of "at least nine deaths and only one chance of survival."

When a stomach ulcer perforates, or after it perforates, the patient will experience intense pain in the upper abdomen, causing great suffering. This condition is a critical type of "acute abdomen." According to the principles of treating "acute abdomen," immediate intervention is necessary. However, what the patient or the patient's family wants is pain relief! Of course, pain relief is necessary, but what method should be used? Taking pain pills? Getting a morphine injection? Smoking opium? The answer is, taking pain pills is useless. A morphine injection or smoking opium can relieve the pain because narcotics can anesthetize the patient's brain, making them unaware of the pain. For example, if someone sees their property on fire, they will be extremely anxious, but if they are anesthetized, they will be calm and unconcerned. However, even if they are mentally at peace and stand idly by, will the fire not still consume their property? Relieving this type of pain with a morphine injection or smoking opium is the same. While it is true that this pain should be relieved, simply relieving the pain is not enough, because if the underlying condition is not treated, the person will die even if they no longer feel the pain.

In simple terms, if a skilled surgeon confirms that a stomach ulcer has perforated, surgical intervention should be performed immediately to close the hole in the stomach, allowing the patient to turn the corner. According to years of surgical experience, there is only a twelve-hour window of opportunity to save the patient's life after a stomach ulcer perforates. After twelve hours, it is considered "nine deaths and only one chance of survival." From the moment of perforation, each passing hour increases the risk, and the longer the time, the greater the danger and the less hope for survival. Under no circumstances should one simply seek pain relief through anesthesia and delay treatment in an attempt to avoid surgery. As a rule, even if surgery is performed after twelve hours of perforation, the hope for survival is very slim. Those with severe stomach pain should pay close attention to this basic scientific knowledge.

Appendicitis Appendicitis is caused by inflammation of the appendix. Appendicitis is a common disease. Europeans and Americans are more likely to suffer from this disease than Chinese people. However, Chinese people still suffer from appendicitis, just not as frequently. The more civilized the lifestyle, the more cases of appendicitis. People in cities are more likely to suffer from it than people in rural areas. The causes of appendicitis are not always the same, but constipation and indigestion are the most important causes. Other pathological details will not be discussed here.

When the appendix becomes inflamed, it will cause pain. This pain often strikes suddenly, like a disaster falling from the sky, coming in waves and being extremely painful. The pain is often located in the abdomen, about two or three inches downward and to the right of the navel. The more acute the inflammation, the more severe the pain. If the inflammation is chronic, the pain will be mild. Sometimes, the intense pain of appendicitis will suddenly stop, and the patient may experience false relief, thinking that the abdominal pain has suddenly healed. However, this is not the case. This symptom is often caused by the inflammation and swelling of the appendix leading to perforation, peritonitis, or the formation of a localized abscess in the abdomen. The most dangerous aspect of appendicitis is the peritonitis caused by the ulceration of the appendix. This type of peritonitis is extremely dangerous, so appendicitis is one of the most important "acute abdominal" conditions.

Common Sense for Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Health 198

— Tang Renjin

(40) Hyperopia (Farsightedness) and Presbyopia (Age-Related Farsightedness)

The Formation of Hyperopia (Farsightedness). Is also the result of the "reasons why the eye can see objects" as described in the previous section. However, it cannot implement the functions of a camera. This type of eye. Also belongs to a type of non-emmetropic (not having normal vision) eyes. In other words. It is an eyeball with an unhealthy vision. Its ability. Only allows for farsightedness. It cannot see up close. This is the complete opposite of nearsightedness. Because its crystalline lens has too little convexity. Or because its axial length (the distance from the front to the back of the eye) is too short. So the images formed by light rays. Although there are the adjustments of the iris contracting and dilating, the refraction of the crystalline lens, and its natural regulatory function. However, it cannot be completely properly projected onto the retina. Instead, it is projected behind the retina (refer to the attached diagram). Therefore, any objects at a close distance. Cannot be seen clearly. With this type of hyperopic eyeball. When reading books, writing, or working at close range. It is of course also necessary to use corrective glasses for assistance. This type of corrective glasses. Is equipped with suitable convex lenses. To change the refractive power of the crystalline lens. In this way, the images refracted by the crystalline lens. Can be completely projected onto the retina. At this time, the eyeball will also become an eye with a healthy emmetropic function. Can clearly see objects at close range. However, before configuring this type of convex lens. It should also be thoroughly checked by an ophthalmologist for the condition of the various parts of the eye. Only then is it appropriate.

The Formation of Presbyopia. Is caused by age-related factors. Because the crystalline lens of the elderly. Can gradually lose moisture. Elasticity also decreases. And it becomes hardened. Therefore, its ability to refract light rays. Also weakens. At the same time, its regulatory function. Also becomes incomplete. The result of having this type of eyeball. Is similar to hyperopia. It also cannot clearly see objects at close range. So when reading books, writing, or working at close range. It is also necessary to have the assistance of corrective glasses. This type of corrective glasses. Is also the reading glasses commonly used by ordinary people.

A Brief Discussion of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (4)(5) 200

— Hu Jiayan

The typical clinical courses of exudative and proliferative forms have been generally described above! However, in reality, the condition of pulmonary tuberculosis is almost always a mixed and unclear one, with both aspects present; purely uniform forms are almost non-existent. Examples of proliferative forms transitioning to exudative forms, and exudative forms becoming proliferative or healing into sclerotic forms, are frequently seen clinically. Even within a single case, all three types of changes—exudative, proliferative, and sclerotic—can coexist. Therefore, it is practically impossible to make a definitive prediction about the prognosis based solely on the patient's examination findings at that time. Patients often fail to understand this point; but if they understand the aforementioned truth, I believe there will be no further questions!

Finally, let me briefly describe the clinical course of the sclerotic form and cavities. The sclerotic form mostly occurs after the proliferative form. Its course is chronic, and the symptoms are not very severe. Sometimes, it is almost indistinguishable from bronchitis. Sometimes, patients experience mild dyspnea and chest pain due to climbing or exercise, which can lead to suspicion of joint inflammation. Physical examinations often yield unremarkable results; there is no fever, and blood tests are also unremarkable, except that tubercle bacilli can sometimes be found in the sputum. The most accurate diagnosis, of course, cannot be made without X-ray fluoroscopy! The prognosis is generally favorable, unless there are concomitant exudative or proliferative changes, which are exceptions.

As for how cavities are formed, it has already been discussed in Chapter 5! At this time, the patient's subjective symptoms are mostly absent; for example, there is no temperature increase, and the blood count is normal. The erythrocyte sedimentation rate is a little faster, but not significantly. The presence of tubercle bacilli and elastic fibers in the sputum, and the detection of tympanic sounds during percussion, are very important for diagnosis. The course is mostly incurable without surgical treatment; the prognosis is also poor. Occasionally, scar formation due to the proliferation of new connective tissue can be seen; but it is rare and takes a very long time. (End of Chapter 9)

Free Talk

On Ballad Novels 201

— Han Feng

Ballad novels are a type of southern peasant literature. Their influence is as great as that of storytelling with drums in the north, as Xi Di said. This is a type of literature that is completely loved and enjoyed by women, commoners, and the illiterate. However, people who study literature have never paid much attention to them, thinking that they "do not count as literature," until recent years, when they have gradually been brought up.

This cannot help but make one feel that Wu Yanren and Li Boyuan had admirable qualities. Although they were both members of the feudal intellectual class, born in the old era, they fully understood the importance of ballad literature. Li Boyuan wrote a six-volume "Ballad of the Boxer Rebellion," which not only opened up a new path of social significance for ballad novels, which had always limited their subject matter to romantic love affairs, but also became the first book of anti-imperialist literature in China in the field of ballads. Although Wu Yanren did not write anything in this regard, he left us with some opinions. In the seventh issue of the second volume of the new novel "Xiaoshuo Conghua," published in the thirty-first year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, there is a section in which he discusses "Ballad Novels," saying:

"Ballad scripts, etc., are called 'wooden fish books' by the Cantonese. Although these wooden fish books are all fabricated and unfounded, their main purpose is to narrate stories of loyalty, filial piety, chastity, and righteousness. Even when telling the story of a prostitute, it must be said that she died for her lover. Other things, such as righteous servants who are executed in place of their masters, and filial daughters who sell themselves to redeem their fathers, are all found at the beginning of the book, and there is nowhere where they are not found, and they must all have a very good ending. Women and girls, who are accustomed to reading these books, are thus secretly educated. It is a pity that these wooden fish books are limited to local dialects and cannot be spread far and wide."

Although Wu Yanren was unable to make a very good assessment of the literary value of ballad novels, he was very clear about the great social influence of such works. He did not condescendingly despise this type of work.

In the printed editions of ballads, almost every one has a preface explaining the great importance of ballads to customs and human hearts, and the large number of listeners and readers. Wu Yanren's views can be taken as representative, except that he discarded the part that "can dispel boredom and alleviate worries." Therefore, the purpose of the emergence of ballad novels is more blatant and unified than that of other types of popular literature, using a musical form to expand the influence of feudal morality. Also, because of this "too unified" reason, all ballad novels inevitably become a type of stereotyped work. Wu Yanren's words also touched on this point.

What are the literary values of ballad novels? According to Xi Di's opinion: "The narration and description in ballads are much more skillful than in popular biographies and the Romance of Sui and Tang Dynasties; even compared to the Red Chamber Dream and the Golden Lotus, which like to narrate trivial matters, they are even more skilled in describing details and emotions in a subtle and thorough manner. In the past, someone told a joke, saying that listening to someone singing a ballad, describing a woman whose shoelace came undone and bending down to tie it, took one or two nights, and the woman's shoelace was still not tied; this of course contains some ridicule, but the meticulous and profound narration of ballads can be seen from this." This "describing details and emotions in a subtle and thorough manner" does indeed illustrate the characteristics of ballads. However, sometimes the authors of ballads use this method improperly, which damages the literary value of the entire book. For example, in "Why Bother with the West Chamber," using five volumes to write a wedding scene, no matter what, cannot help but make the listeners and readers feel drowsy.

Speaking of "Why Bother with the West Chamber," I am reminded of Tongfeng Waishi's words on "blind ballads," he said: "I don't know when blind ballads began, but there is still a legacy of reciting in a singsong manner. Yuan Qu Cunzhai's poem on passing through Bianliang:

'Blind girls on the street have endless sorrows,

They can strum the pipa and tell the story of the Zhao family,' is the same as 'competing to sing the song of Cai Zhonglang along the street.' Also, Song Lu Fangweng: 'In the Zhao Family Village under the setting sun and ancient willows, a blind old man with a lute is performing.' Blind ballads have been around for a long time. If their new melodies are elegant and can be sung, and they follow the beat like a little Qin King's tune, they are no less than songs written by village schoolteachers in seven-character verse, just to elicit laughter."

This is a historical account of ballad novels, and an explanation of their literary value. Ballad novels, like other literary works, are divided into good and bad depending on the author's cultivation. The best ones move freely between poetry, lyrics, and songs, and are both popular and elegant, and the success of the book "Poetic Hairpin" is one example.

We often divide general novels into long, medium, and short stories, and ballad novels are the same. Xi Di said that some ballad novels are as many as forty volumes, and the trilogy together can exceed seventy volumes. I once saw a manuscript called "Pomegranate Flower Dream," which was as many as three hundred volumes, which can be called the largest work in ballad novels. According to Xi Di, there is a printed edition of this book in Fujian, but I don't know how many volumes the printed book has. Generally, long ballad novels are always over thirty volumes, medium-length ones such as "Heavenly Rain of Flowers" are over ten volumes, and short books such as "Why Bother with the West Chamber" with four, five, seven, or eight volumes, such as "Returning the Golden Gong," can only be considered short stories. In addition, there is a type of "opening chapter," and those contained in "Poetic Hairpin" are only scattered short chapters.

Determined by the stereotyped subject matter and form, ballad novels, like feudal forces, have gradually been heading towards a dead end. Although Li Boyuan tried hard to open up a new direction, and although the September 18th and January 28th incidents also produced some new "opening chapters," in fact, they still could not develop very well. So, where will Chinese ballad novels go in the future? Due to the continuation of inherent influences, there is probably still a need to retain this form and transform it, but in the future, its existence will ultimately be lost, and this is a prediction that anyone can make.

War and Peace 202

— Hu Yifan

War is a primitive, cruel killing, which is commonly known. From ancient texts and poems, we have already seen many such tragic faces that are shocking. Such as "Elegy for an Ancient Battlefield," and "Pitiful are the bones by the River of Unrest, Still dreaming of their loved ones in spring chambers," "Better to be a dog in times of peace, than a human in times of turmoil," and so on. These popular articles and poems, after reading, will make people clearly think of the scaly white bones in the aftermath of the flames of war, the desolate scenes of destroyed tiles and scorched earth, the sad lives of orphaned widows separated from their loved ones in life and death. All of this will naturally and easily arouse people's feelings of aversion to war, and forget who the creators and instigators of war are. In other words, they have become unaware of why there is war; but when war comes, it gives them only such pain and destruction, so they have no choice but to simply hate war and curse war. Thus, knowing that war is inevitable and will come, but with the knife already at their throats, they still cannot help but fantasize and rave about peace. The same erroneous thought, because of the hatred and pain for war, even sees the normal self-defense war and resistance war of their own people as a sin, as something that should not exist. As an example of the former, we can look at the "praying for peace" and other things that have been popular in the past year or two; as an example of the latter, we can also see the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom of not so distant times, the so-called "rebellious long-haired bandits," which is already a sign.

It is true that war can kill people, but if used well, it can also save people. For example, this type of war, like "better to have one family cry than a whole road cry," is not only necessary, but it must be that fewer people die and more people live, which is worth adopting. Conversely, it is also true that peace can save people, but if the direction is wrong, peace can still kill people. For example, supporting the peace of "why have one family cry when a whole road can cry" is very undesirable; going on with that kind of peace will inevitably lead to very few people living and more people dying. This kind of peace should not only be cursed, but also rejected.

Here, therefore, a kind of understanding is needed: blind anti-war and blind warfare are both insufficient for training. When war comes, the courage to recognize it should precede fear: ask why this war came? For others or for oneself? When the recognition is clear, then one dares to advocate peace, and one will not be blindly deceived and await execution.

Therefore, when talking about anti-war, if the interests truly involve the weaker party themselves, it is not enough to simply pray for peace, but only to use war to stop war, and seek survival from death. Otherwise, one can only "the fittest survive, natural selection," and await execution.

Humorous Song 203

— TK

Viewing Plum Blossoms at Yoshino 204

— Zhao Qi

(Part 1)

About twenty of us formed a group and took the streetcar to Shinjuku Station at 8:15. We then bought round-trip tickets for viewing plum blossoms at Yoshino for 1.20 yen and squeezed into the train car with the swarm of tourists. The air was stuffy for a moment. After we settled down, unexpectedly, a continuous drizzle started. People on the train grumbled "dame dame" (meaning "terrible"), but I felt that appreciating plum blossoms in the rain had its own unique charm. However, before long, the heavy, damp air transformed back into patches of clear, sunny clouds.

The Yoshino Plum Orchard is the only famous scenic spot near Tokyo. Every year during the peak bloom season, special trains are arranged for sightseeing. Tourists continuously visit from mid-February until late March. The Japanese have a deep and refined interest in spring outings. Especially the women, they feel ashamed if they lack a beautiful parasol and telescope at this time. Ordinary people gather their families and bring picnic supplies. Elderly scholars often bring writing brushes, inkstones, and wine bottles to search for poetic inspiration.

The local train didn't stop at any station, simply pulling us further into the colors of early spring. After passing Mount Tachikawa, its back covered in lingering snow, the first thing we saw was the ice plum blossoms that I had dreamed of for many years. At this moment, the joyful outline in my heart was just like the faces of those who had just seen the sunny and rainy weather. Hesitantly, at first, one or two trees flashed by, then they gradually became denser, lined up on both sides of the elegant, low houses, coated with a layer of dazzling silver by the sunlight. A warm and soft breeze entered through the window, and people were bathed in the cool fragrance. An old man wearing a red woolen hat in the next seat was surrounded and urged to drink wine, and children were constantly sniffing loudly.

Past here is Qingmei Station. You can walk to the plum orchard after getting off the train. However, the train ticket indicates that there are three places where you can get off and go there, meaning there are still Hinata-Wada and Raku Raku-en stations ahead. In order not to miss any beautiful places, we finally got off at the last station. It seemed that most of the people on the train also got off here. (To be continued)

After Dusk 205

— Wu Guanglue

Night.

The gray-black curtain can cover the moonlight and starlight. Under the dim flashes revealed in the haze, the earth is just a patch of darkness, a hazy scene. After the villagers hastily ate their dinner in the kitchen, they abruptly rushed out the gate and gathered with neighboring brothers to chat leisurely and hopefully throw themselves into the embrace of the vast nature to recuperate their tired bodies. So on the grassy slopes and on the open ground, chairs and stools were placed in twos and threes, and crowds gathered. The night breeze, like the faint breath of a ghost, gently blows across people's dry, haggard faces, showing signs of fatigue.

"Oh... Oh..."

In the midst of people's conversations, occasionally a sorrowful, deep sigh would escape. The melancholy and mournful tone was like the faint breath of an old mill donkey, tired from a full day's work, quietly lying down to rest.

But nature is ultimately benevolent, charitable, and philanthropic to mankind: after a period of quiet rest, people are like the earth turning from darkness to dawn, seemingly endowed with life anew by the Creator, displaying a lively and joyful scene. People temporarily forget their fatigue and chat and laugh cheerfully. The old man recalls the peaceful and prosperous times of the past, earnestly and vividly narrating to the younger generation: how easy it was to live in the past, two copper coins could buy a box of matches, thirty coins could buy a pound of pork, and dozens of coins could let you sit in a tavern for half a day... But now, the world has changed! Pork costs several dimes a pound, matches cost more than ten coins a box, and going to a tavern requires several dimes just to have a little something to eat and drink... In the end, he naturally shakes his head and sighs with emotion: "Each generation is worse than the last. It's really not easy to live..."

"The price of rice has gone up again!"

Suddenly, someone exclaimed in a corner. Upon hearing this, the crowd trembled as if struck by lightning, sighing incessantly. Naturally, they were threatened by this sudden news and worried and saddened about their vague prospects in life.

"What can we do?" They sigh, sigh, sigh deeply, mournfully and hoarsely.

The atmosphere returns to silence. People sit silently and worriedly, like a herd of tired cattle in a waiting room, breathing and sobbing in the boundless darkness. This is the symbol of their lives.

Four Women and a Wristwatch 206

— Fan Hai

In a dark and desolate forest

There is a muddy, winding path,

The path disappears into the forest, casting black shadows,

Suddenly, three young women walk out,

Their faces covered with headscarves,

Aprons of work hanging from their chests.

They stretch their necks,

Their hands are held behind them

The cart immediately follows them

Out of the shadows behind them,

A middle-aged woman is sitting on that cart,

Her dark brown face breaks into a smile;

In the darkness, you can only hear

In the gray, cold air, the shrill

Little birds are screaming snow in the dead forest.

The cart lightly jumps on the withered grass,

The cart lightly jumps on the uneven yellow earth,

The desolate, silent forest

The lead-black sky opens cold eyes

Through the branches and leaves,

See their smiling mouths,

Chatting lips, frostbitten cheeks.

Miscellaneous Notes on War (10) 207

— By Tokunaga Sunao, translated by Ye Yin

In the evening, I definitely read it aloud two or three times for people to hear. The second portion of leftover rice was brought, and the people nearby, like Brother Aji who sells brushes, Brother Achong who buys ashes, Brother A Xiong with one hand, etc., some took the rice back home and then came back; some sat in a row on the door frame, putting the rice and soup together in the wooden bowls with peeling paint that they had left there in advance, eating while listening to me passionately reciting the romance. — This has become their habit.

When I was a fourth-grade student, I was already an expert on romances in the school. I remember once this happened. A male student named Konmatsu, who was very influential in our class, drew a picture of Kato Kiyomasa fighting with Kiyama Danjo and falling off a cliff, showing it off to everyone. However, the class leader of the fifth grade, named Yonemura, spoke up, saying: That's not Kiyama Danjo, but Shiohten Tanba-no-Kami. Since it couldn't be determined whether it was Kiyama Danjo or Shiohten Tanba-no-Kami, Konmatsu's group of about thirty people and Yonemura's group of about twenty-five or six people clashed, arguing that it was Kiyama on one side and Shiohten on the other, each sticking to their own opinions, almost turning into a fight. Therefore, the clever guys in the class skipped class and specially ran to my house to pick me up, saying that they wanted me to be the judge. So, I carried my younger brother as usual, ran to where everyone was, and explained "It's Kiyama Danjo"; and I also explained: Kiyama was originally stronger than Kiyomasa, and Kiyomasa was first pushed to the ground: but when he fell off the cliff, his helmet was entangled by vines, and he took the opportunity to turn over and kill the opponent. Thus, our group won, and everyone supported me and was very happy; but on the way back, when I was alone, I was surrounded by students from Yonemura's group and beaten black and blue.

Brother Xiong with one hand, Brother Afeng with a red cloth around his waist, Brother Aji who sells brushes, Brother Achong who buys ashes, etc., all lived in my house.

These are all people that I can never forget in my life. The older I get, the more clearly I can judge things, the more I can't help but think of these people.
